2:23:1201:0:14:72:276:698:12:Times:12:Times:Preference Signaling in Matching Markets
2:24:1241:14:14:72:313:684:12:Times:12:Times:Peter Coles, Alexey Kushnir, and Muriel Niederle
2:25:1289:14:14:72:234:670:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 16185
2:26:1317:14:14:72:228:656:12:Times:12:Times:July 2010, Revised August 2010
2:27:1347:14:28:72:155:642:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. C78,J01
2:28:1362:28:28:273:338:614:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:29:1370:28:14:72:540:586:12:Times:12:Times:Many labor markets share three stylized facts: employers cannot give full attention to all candidates,
2:30:1472:14:14:72:540:572:12:Times:12:Times:candidates are ready to provide information about their preferences for particular employers, and employers
2:31:1579:14:14:72:540:558:12:Times:12:Times:value and are prepared to act on this information. In this paper we study how a signaling mechanism,
2:32:1679:14:14:72:540:544:12:Times:12:Times:where each worker can send a signal of interest to one employer, facilitates matches in such markets.
2:33:1780:14:14:72:540:530:12:Times:12:Times:We find that introducing a signaling mechanism increases the welfare of workers and the number of
2:34:1877:14:14:72:540:516:12:Times:12:Times:matches, while the change in firm welfare is ambiguous. A signaling mechanism adds the most value
2:35:1974:14:42:72:176:502:12:Times:12:Times:for balanced markets.
2:36:1995:42:14:72:127:460:12:Times:12:Times:Peter Coles
2:37:2006:14:14:72:165:446:12:Times:12:Times:Harvard University
2:38:2024:14:28:72:151:432:12:Times:12:Times:pcoles@hbs.edu
2:39:2038:28:14:72:148:404:12:Times:12:Times:Alexey Kushnir
2:40:2052:14:14:72:198:390:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:41:2075:14:14:72:238:376:12:Times:12:Times:The Pennsylvania State University
2:42:2108:14:0:72:204:362:12:Times:12:Times:alexey.kushnir@gmail.com
2:43:2132:0:14:306:383:460:12:Times:12:Times:Muriel Niederle
2:44:2147:14:14:306:432:446:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:45:2170:14:14:306:378:432:12:Times:12:Times:579 Serra Mall
2:46:2184:14:14:306:401:418:12:Times:12:Times:Stanford University
2:47:2203:14:14:306:431:404:12:Times:12:Times:Stanford, CA 94305-6072
2:48:2226:14:14:306:358:390:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:49:2234:14:278:306:415:376:12:Times:12:Times:niederle@stanford.edu
2:50:2255:278:14:72:239:98:12:Times:12:Times:An online appendix is available at:
2:51:2290:14:0:72:283:84:12:Times:12:Times:http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w16185
3:52:2330:0:30:72:208:708:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:1    Introduction
3:53:2347:30:18:72:540:678:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Job  seekers  in  labor  markets  often  apply  for  many  positions,  as  there  is  a  low  cost  for
3:54:2450:18:18:72:540:660:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:applying  and  a  high  value  for  being  employed.   Consequently,  many  employers  face  the
3:55:2546:18:18:72:540:642:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:near impossible task of reviewing and evaluating hundreds of applications.  Moreover, since
3:56:2637:18:18:72:540:624:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:pursuing  candidates  is  often  costly,  employers  may  need  to  assess  not  only  the  quality  of
3:57:2740:18:18:72:540:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:an applicant, but also whether the applicant is attainable:  that is, whether the candidate
3:58:2831:18:18:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is likely to ultimately accept a job offer, should the employer make one.  In this paper we
3:59:2922:18:18:72:540:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:study a mechanism that aids employers in this evaluation process by allowing applicants to
3:60:3012:18:18:72:401:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:credibly signal information about their preferences for positions.
3:61:3078:18:18:89:539:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In practice, in many markets that suffer from this form of application congestion, can-
3:62:3165:18:17:72:540:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:didates communicate special interest for a select number of places.  For example, in college
3:63:3257:17:18:72:540:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:admissions in the United States,  many universities have early admission programs,  where
3:64:3346:18:18:72:540:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:high school seniors may apply to exactly one college before the general application period.
3:65:3437:18:18:72:540:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Evidence suggests that universities respond to such action in that it is easier to get into a
3:66:3530:18:18:72:539:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:college through early admission programs (Avery,  Fairbanks and Zeckhauser, 2003).1An-
3:67:3616:18:18:71:539:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other  example  of  applicants  signaling  interest  can  be  found  in  the  market  for  entry-level
3:68:3718:18:18:71:539:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:clinical psychologists, which in the early 1990’s was organized as a telephone-based market.
3:69:3810:18:18:71:539:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:On “match day,” program directors called applicants to make offers, and candidates were,
3:70:3898:18:18:71:539:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:at  any  moment,  allowed  to  hold  on  to  at  most  one  offer.   At  the  end  of  match  day,  all
3:71:4001:18:18:71:539:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-accepted offers were automatically declared as rejected.  Due in part to its limited time
3:72:4094:18:18:71:539:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:frame,  this market suffered from congestion,  and it was common for program directors to
3:73:4183:18:18:71:539:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:make offers out of their preference order to applicants who credibly indicated they would
3:74:4272:18:18:71:341:301:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:accept an offer immediately (Roth and Xing, 1997).2
3:75:4323:18:18:89:539:283:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Some  markets  have  formal,  market-wide  mechanisms  that  allow  participants  to  signal
3:76:4415:18:17:71:539:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preferences, and the formal nature of the signals ensures credibility.  Since 2006, The Ameri-
3:77:4509:17:19:71:539:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:can Economic Association (AEA) has operated a signaling service to facilitate the job search
3:78:4601:19:16:85:539:229:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:1Under single early application programs, universities often require that an applicant not apply early to
3:79:4706:16:12:72:540:213:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:other schools, and this is often enforced by high school guidance counselors.  In another example of colleges
3:80:4815:12:11:72:540:201:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:looking for signs of interest, many schools take great care to note whether applicants visit the campus, which
3:81:4925:11:12:72:540:190:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:presumably is costly for parents in terms of time and money.  This can also be taken into account when
3:82:5027:12:9:72:208:178:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:colleges decide whom to admit.
3:83:5057:9:15:85:539:169:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:2Congestion in the telephone market was costly for program directors who worried that their offer would
3:84:5160:15:12:72:540:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:be  held  the  whole  match  day  and  then  rejected  in  the  last  moments,  leaving  them  to  fill  the  position  in
3:85:5282:12:12:72:540:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:a hectic “aftermarket” with only a few leftover candidates.  As an example of offer strategy, the directors
3:86:5389:12:12:72:540:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of one internship program decided to make their first offers (for their five positions) to numbers 1, 2, 3, 5,
3:87:5499:12:12:72:540:118:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:and 12 on their rank-order list of candidates, with the rationale that 3, 5, and 12 had indicated that they
3:88:5606:12:12:72:540:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:would accept immediately and that 1 and 2 were so attractive as to be worth taking chances on.  Anecdotal
3:89:5711:12:12:72:540:94:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:evidence suggests that promises to accept an offer were binding.  The market was relatively small, and as
3:90:5816:12:0:72:347:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:one program director mentioned:  “you see these people again.”
4:91:5879:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for economics graduate students.  Using this service, students can send signals to up to two
4:92:5971:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:employers  to  indicate  their  interest  in  receiving  an  interview  at  the  annual  Allied  Social
4:93:6074:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Science Associations meeting.  Coles et al. (2010) provide suggestive evidence that sending a
4:94:6167:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signal of interest increases the chances of receiving an interview.  Since interviews take place
4:95:6263:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:over a single weekend, departments typically interview about twenty candidates out of hun-
4:96:6353:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:dreds of applicants, which suggests that most departments must strategically choose from
4:97:6441:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:among their candidates that are above the bar.3Though not labor markets,  some online
4:98:6526:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:dating websites allow participants to send signals to potential partners.  For example in the
4:99:6619:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:matchmaking service of the website “Hot or Not,” participants can send each other virtual
4:100:6708:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:flowers  that  purportedly  increase  the  chances  of  receiving  a  positive  response.4In  a  field
4:101:6810:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:experiment on a major Korean online dating website, Lee et al. (2009) study the effect of a
4:102:6901:18:18:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:user attaching one of a limited number of “virtual roses” to a date request.  They find that
4:103:6993:18:18:71:530:492:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:users of both genders are more likely to accept a request when a virtual rose is attached.5
4:104:7084:18:17:89:539:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:These examples all share three important features. First, in each case substantial frictions
4:105:7176:17:18:71:539:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:lead to market congestion:  employers (or colleges or dating partners) are unable to give full
4:106:7270:18:18:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:attention  to  all  possible  candidates  when  making  decisions.   Second,  applicants  are  ready
4:107:7370:18:18:71:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to provide information about their preferences over employers.  Third, employers value this
4:108:7461:18:18:71:342:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preference information and are prepared to act on it.
4:109:7514:18:18:89:539:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:For  employers  to  take  useful  action,  preference  signals  must  be  credible.   But  simply
4:110:7611:18:18:71:539:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:declaring one’s interest typically bears almost no cost, and job seekers have an incentive to
4:111:7704:18:18:71:539:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:indicate  particular  interest  to  many  employers,  regardless  of  how  strong  their  preferences
4:112:7805:18:18:71:539:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:towards these employers actually are.  Hence,  absent any credibility guarantee,  employers
4:113:7896:18:18:71:539:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:may struggle to discern which preference information is sincere and which is simply cheap
4:114:7985:18:18:71:539:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:talk.   So  while  candidates  may  wish  to  signal  their  preferences,  and  employers  may  value
4:115:8086:18:15:85:539:277:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:3Similar  mechanisms  exist  for  non-academic  jobs.   For  example,  Skydeck360,  a  student-operated  com-
4:116:8195:15:12:72:540:262:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:pany at Harvard,  offers a signaling service for MBA students in their search for internships and full-time
4:117:8302:12:12:72:540:250:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:jobs.   Each  registered  student  can  send  up  to  ten  signals  to  employers  via  their  secure  website.   (See
4:118:8420:12:8:72:266:238:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:http://skydeck360.posterous.com for detail.)
4:119:8464:8:16:85:539:230:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:4In this case the number of flowers one may send is unlimited, but each flower is costly.  Signals of interest
4:120:8574:16:12:72:540:214:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:may be helpful in dating markets because pursuing partners is costly.  At the very least, each user may be
4:121:8680:12:12:72:540:202:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:limited  in  the  number  of  serious  dates  she  can  have  in  a  given  period.   “As  James  Hong  from  HotorNot
4:122:8798:12:12:72:540:190:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:tells it, his virtual flower service has three components:  there’s the object itself represented by a graphical
4:123:8910:12:12:72:540:178:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:flower icon, there’s the gesture of someone sending the flower to their online crush, and finally, there’s the
4:124:9020:12:12:72:540:166:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:trophy  effect  of  everyone  else  being  able  to  see  that  you  got  a  flower.   People  on  HotorNot  are  paying
4:125:9140:12:12:72:540:154:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:$10 to send the object of their affection a virtual flower – which is a staggering 3-4x what you might pay
4:126:9246:12:12:72:540:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:for a real flower!” (from http://www.viralblog.com/research/why-digital-consumers-buy-virtual-goods/) See
4:127:9351:12:8:72:528:130:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:http://www.hotornot.com/m/?flowerBrochure=1 for a description of HotorNot’s virtual flower offerings.
4:128:9452:8:16:85:539:122:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:5This dating website targets people looking for marriage partners, rather than people who want many
4:129:9551:16:12:72:540:106:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:dates.   Hence,  dates  may  be  perceived  as  particularly  costly,  so  users  must  decide  carefully  on  whom  to
4:130:9670:12:12:72:540:94:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:“spend” a date.  The study found that candidates of average attractiveness, who may worry that date offers
4:131:9776:12:0:72:420:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:are only “safety” offers, are particularly responsive to signals of special interest.
5:132:9862:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:learning  candidate  preferences,  inability  to  credibly  convey  information  may  prevent  any
5:133:9960:18:18:72:336:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:gains from preference signaling from being realized.
5:134:10012:18:18:89:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this paper, we investigate how asignaling mechanismthat limits the number of signals
5:135:10099:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a job seeker may send can overcome the credibility problem and improve the welfare of market
5:136:10191:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:participants.  We develop a model that can account for the three stylized facts mentioned
5:137:10280:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:above.  In our model, firms make offers to workers, but the number of offers they may make
5:138:10370:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is limited,  so that firms must carefully select the workers to whom they make offers.  We
5:139:10460:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:focus on the strategic question of offer choice and abstract away the question of acquiring
5:140:10551:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:information that determines preferences.  Hence, we assume that each agent knows her own
5:141:10639:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preferences over agents on the other side of the market, but is uncertain of the preferences
5:142:10731:18:18:72:151:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of other agents.
5:143:10747:18:18:89:539:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In the simplest version of our model, we assume that both worker and firm preferences
5:144:10832:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are idiosyncratic and uniformly distributed.  Workers have the opportunity to send a signal
5:145:10923:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to one firm, where each signal is binary in nature and does not transmit any further infor-
5:146:11014:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mation.  Firms observe their signals, but not the signals of other firms, and then each firm
5:147:11106:18:18:72:540:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:simultaneously makes exactly one offer to a worker.  Finally, workers choose offers from those
5:148:11200:18:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:available to them.  We focus on symmetric equilibria in anonymous strategies to eliminate
5:149:11289:18:18:72:371:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:any coordination devices beyond the signaling mechanism.
5:150:11345:18:18:89:539:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  show  that,  in  expectation,  introducing  a  signaling  mechanism  increases  both  the
5:151:11438:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number  of  matches  as  well  as  the  welfare  of  workers.   Intuitively,  when  firms  make  offers
5:152:11541:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to workers who send them signals, these offers are unlikely to overlap, leading to a higher
5:153:11632:18:18:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expected number of matches.  Furthermore, workers are not only more likely to be matched,
5:154:11721:18:18:72:540:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:but are also more likely to be matched to a firm they prefer the most.  On the other hand,
5:155:11811:18:18:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:when a firm makes an offer to a worker who has signaled it, this creates strong competition
5:156:11902:18:18:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for firms who would like to make an offer to that same worker because, for example, they
5:157:11990:18:18:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:rank that worker highest.  Hence, by responding to signals, that is, being more likely to make
5:158:12084:18:17:72:540:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offers to workers who have signaled them, firms may generate a negative spillover on other
5:159:12174:17:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms.   Consequently,  the  effect  on  firm  welfare  from  introducing  a  signaling  mechanism
5:160:12272:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is  ambiguous;  welfare  for  a  firm  depends  on  the  balance  between  individual  benefit  from
5:161:12372:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:responding  to  signals  and  the  negative  spillover  generated  by  other  firms  responding  to
5:162:12471:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals.  Furthermore, we show that the degree to which a firm responds to signals is a case
5:163:12563:18:18:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of strategic complements.  When one firm responds more to signals, it becomes riskier for
5:164:12652:18:18:72:540:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firms to make offers to workers who have not sent them signals.  Consequently, multiple
5:165:12745:18:18:72:540:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibria, with varying responsiveness to signals, may exist.  These equilibria can be welfare
5:166:12840:18:18:72:540:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ranked:  workers prefer equilibria where firms respond more to signals, while firms prefer the
5:167:12934:18:0:72:249:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibria where they respond less.
6:168:12970:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We also study an extension in which workers have correlated preferences.  In this setting
6:169:13059:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a worker may not necessarily signal to her overall most preferred firm.  This implies that
6:170:13149:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms cannot be certain that an offer made to a worker who sent a signal will be accepted.
6:171:13239:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Nonetheless, for a class of correlated preferences we show that the introduction of a signaling
6:172:13334:18:18:72:489:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mechanism increases the expected number of matches and the welfare of workers.
6:173:13412:18:18:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To understand when a signaling mechanism might be most helpful, we compare perfor-
6:174:13494:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mance across market settings.  To do this, we focus on a simpler environment where agents
6:175:13583:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:care about getting a match,  but not the quality of the match.  Hence,  the value of intro-
6:176:13674:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ducing  a  signaling  mechanism  is  simply  the  expected  increase  in  the  number  of  matches.
6:177:13773:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:For such an environment, we find that the value of a signaling mechanism is maximal for
6:178:13860:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:balanced markets; that is, markets where the number of firms and workers are of roughly the
6:179:13951:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:same magnitude.  We further show that the increase in the number of matches is roughly
6:180:14037:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:homogenous of degree one in the number of firms and workers.  That is, signaling mechanisms
6:181:14128:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are equally important for large and small markets in terms of the expected increase in the
6:182:14218:17:18:72:240:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fraction of matched participants.
6:183:14251:18:18:89:539:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Our  approach  is  related  to  several  strands  of  literature.   A  standard  interpretation  of
6:184:14350:18:18:72:540:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signaling and its effectiveness is that applicants have private information that is pertinent
6:185:14443:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to  how  valuable  an  employee  they  would  be.   For  example,  in  Spence’s  signaling  model
6:186:14540:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(Spence,  1973),  applicants  use  wasteful  costly  signals,  such  as  education,  to  signal  their
6:187:14642:18:18:72:539:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:type, such as their ability.6More recently, Avery and Levin (2009) model early application
6:188:14732:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in  US  college  admissions  as  a  way  for  students  to  signal  college-specific  quality,  such  as
6:189:14836:18:18:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:enthusiasm  for  a  particular  college.   In  their  model,  colleges  explicitly  derive  more  utility
6:190:14941:18:18:72:540:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from having enthusiastic students in their freshman class than they do from other, equally
6:191:15031:18:18:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:able students.  By contrast, in our model we abstract away from such motives and instead
6:192:15119:18:18:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:show how congestion, stemming from the explicit monetary or opportunity costs of making
6:193:15206:18:18:72:360:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offers, can generate room for useful preference signaling.
6:194:15264:18:17:89:539:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A more closely related strand of literature is that of strategic information transmission,
6:195:15354:17:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:or “cheap talk,” between a sender and receiver, introduced in Crawford and Sobel (1982).
6:196:15442:18:18:72:540:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In our model,  however,  we consider a multi-stage game with many senders (workers) and
6:197:15529:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:many receivers (firms), where the structure of allowable signals plays a distinctive role.  Each
6:198:15625:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sender must choose the receiver to whom she will send one of her limited, identical signals,
6:199:15717:18:18:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the scarcity of signals induces credibility.  Each receiver knows only whether a sender has
6:200:15812:18:18:72:540:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sent a signal to it or not, and receives no additional information.  While Crawford and Sobel
6:201:15905:18:16:85:539:116:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:6Hoppe, Moldovanu and Sela (2009) extend this idea to an environment where agents on both sides of the
6:202:16007:16:11:72:540:100:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:market may send signals.  Among other findings, they identify general conditions under which the potential
6:203:16113:11:0:72:498:89:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:increase in expected output due to the introduction of signaling is offset by the costs of signaling.
7:204:16215:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(1982) study a coordination problem between the sender and receiver, our setting includes an
7:205:16307:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:additional coordination problem among receivers who must decide whom to make an offer.
7:206:16393:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Nevertheless, some features of Crawford and Sobel persist in our model.  Signals are “cheap”
7:207:16485:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in the sense that they do not have a direct influence on agent payoffs.  Each agent has only a
7:208:16579:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:limited number of signals, so there is an opportunity cost associated with sending a signal.
7:209:16671:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Finally,  in  our  model  there  always  exist  babbling  equilibria  where  agents  ignore  signals;
7:210:16772:18:18:72:512:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:hence, the introduction of a signaling mechanism always enlarges the set of equilibria.
7:211:16859:18:18:89:539:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While to our knowledge we are the first to introduce preference signaling in decentralized
7:212:16949:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:markets,  papers by Abdulkadiroglu,  Che and Yasuda (2008) and Lee and Schwarz (2007)
7:213:17034:18:18:72:460:546:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:deal with preference signaling in the presence of centralized clearinghouses.7
7:214:17112:18:18:89:539:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In  summary,  our  paper  models  the  introduction  of  a  signaling  mechanism  in  markets
7:215:17205:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:where interviews or offers are costly for firms, either in direct monetary terms or because of
7:216:17299:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:opportunity costs.  Our results suggest potentially large welfare gains for workers,  and an
7:217:17391:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:increase in the expected total number of matches.  Furthermore, as the experience with the
7:218:17481:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:economic job market shows, introducing a signaling mechanism can be a low cost, unintrusive
7:219:17572:18:18:72:540:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:means of improving maket outcomes.  As such we see our paper as part of the larger market
7:220:17661:18:18:72:248:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:design literature (c.f.  Roth, 2008).
7:221:17698:18:18:89:539:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The paper proceeds as follows.  Section 2 begins with a simple example, and Sections 3
7:222:17784:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and 4 discuss the offer game with and without a signaling mechanism, respectively.  Section
7:223:17875:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5 considers the impact of introducing a signaling mechanism on the welfare of agents.  In
7:224:17964:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Section 6 we examine signaling in an environment with correlated agent preferences.  Section
7:225:18056:18:18:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:7 analyzes the robustness of the welfare results across various market structures.  Section 8
7:226:18149:18:45:72:124:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:concludes.
7:227:18159:45:30:72:259:268:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:2    A Simple Example
7:228:18180:30:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this section we lay out a simple example that shows the effects of introducing a signaling
7:229:18273:18:18:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mechanism  and  highlights  some  of  our  main  findings.   Consider  a  market  with  two  firms
7:230:18371:18:18:72:539:202:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:{f1,f2}and  two  workers{w1,w2}.   For  each  agent,  a  match  with  one’s  most  preferred
7:231:18463:18:18:72:540:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:partner from the other side of the market yields payoff 1, while a match with one’s second
7:232:18553:18:18:72:432:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:choice partner yieldsx∈(0,1).  Remaining unmatched yields payoff 0.
7:233:18620:18:16:85:539:148:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:7Abdulkadiroglu, Che and Yasuda (2008) show that the introduction of a signaling technology improves
7:234:18720:16:12:72:540:132:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:efficiency of the deferred acceptance algorithm in a school choice problem.  Lee and Schwarz (2007) analyze
7:235:18827:12:12:72:540:120:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:preference signaling in a match formation process between firms and workers that consists of three steps:
7:236:18932:12:11:72:540:108:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:preference signaling, investments in information acquisition, and formation of matches via a centralized clear-
7:237:19043:11:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:inghouse.  They construct a centralized mechanism where workers communicate their complete preferences
7:238:19145:12:0:72:508:85:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:to an intermediary, and the intermediary recommends to each firm a subset of workers to interview.
8:239:19244:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Ex-ante, agent preferences are random, uniform and independent.  That is, for each firm
8:240:19331:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:f, the probability thatfprefers workerw1to workerw2is one half, as is the probability
8:241:19416:18:18:72:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:thatfprefersw2tow1.  Worker preferences over firms are similarly symmetric.  Agents learn
8:242:19505:18:18:71:389:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:their own preferences, but not the preferences of other agents.
8:243:19568:18:18:89:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We first examine behavior in a game where once agent preferences are realized, each firm
8:244:19656:18:18:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:may  make  a  single  offer  to  a  worker.   Workers  then  accept  at  most  one  of  their  available
8:245:19760:18:18:71:539:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offers.   We  will  examine  sequential  equilibria,  which  guarantees  that  workers  accept  their
8:246:19861:18:18:71:170:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:best available offer.
8:247:19882:18:18:89:539:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In the unique equilibrium of this game where firm strategies do not depend on the name
8:248:19968:18:18:71:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of the worker,8each firm simply makes an offer to its most preferred worker.  This follows
8:249:20058:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:because firms cannot discern which worker is more likely to accept an offer.  In this congested
8:250:20153:18:18:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:market there is a fifty percent chance that both firms make an offer to the same worker, in
8:251:20244:18:18:71:539:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which case there will only be one match.  Hence, on average there are 1.5 matches, and the
8:252:20334:18:17:71:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expected payoff for each firm is341 +140 = 0.75.  For workers, if they receive exactly one offer,
8:253:20431:17:18:71:539:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:it is equally likely to be from their first or second choice firm.  There is also a fifty percent
8:254:20528:18:18:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:chance that one worker receives two offers, hence attaining a payoff of one while the other
8:255:20619:18:18:71:461:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:worker receives zero.  The expected payoff for each worker is then (2 +x)/4.
8:256:20695:18:18:89:539:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  now  introduce  a  signaling  mechanism:  before  firms  make  offers,  each  worker  may
8:257:20788:18:18:71:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:send asignalto a single firm.  Each signal has a binary nature:  either a firm receives a signal
8:258:20884:18:18:71:539:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from a particular worker or not, and signals do not not transmit any other information.  We
8:259:20975:18:18:71:539:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:focus on non-babbling equilibria, where firms interpret a signal as a sign of being the more
8:260:21067:18:18:71:510:331:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:preferred firm of that worker, and workers send a signal to their more preferred firm.9
8:261:21154:18:18:89:539:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To analyze firm behavior, note that a firm that receives a signal from its top worker will
8:262:21244:18:18:71:539:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:make this worker an offer, since it will certainly be accepted.  If on the other hand a firm
8:263:21336:18:18:71:539:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:receives no signals, it again optimally makes an offer to its top worker, as symmetry implies
8:264:21429:18:18:71:539:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the workers are equally likely to accept an offer.  The interesting strategic decision a firm
8:265:21522:18:17:71:539:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:must make is when it receives a signal only from its second ranked worker.  In this case the
8:266:21614:17:18:71:539:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firm also receives exactly one signal.  We say a firm “responds” to the signal if it makes
8:267:21710:18:18:71:539:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the signaling worker an offer, and “ignores” the signal if it instead makes an offer to its top
8:268:21805:18:18:71:268:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worker, which did not send it a signal.
8:269:21844:18:18:89:539:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Supposef1prefersw1tow2and  onlyw2sent  a  signal  tof1,  which  impliesw1sent  a
8:270:21924:18:12:85:356:152:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:8See Section 3 for a formal definition of anonymous strategies.
8:271:21987:12:16:85:539:140:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:9Note  that  there  is  no  equilibrium  where  firms  expect  signals  from  workers,  but  interpret  them  as  a
8:272:22102:16:12:72:540:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:particular lack of interest and hence reduce the probability of making an offer to a signaling worker.  If this
8:273:22213:12:12:72:540:112:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:were the case, workers would simply not send any signal.  There are, however, babbling equilibria where no
8:274:22319:12:12:72:540:100:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:information is transmitted, though we will not focus on those in this paper, as they are equivalent to not
8:275:22425:12:0:72:184:88:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:having a signaling device.
9:276:22452:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signal tof2.Clearly,  wheneverf1makes an offer tow2,f1receivesx.Supposef1instead
9:277:22532:18:18:72:539:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:makes an offer tow1, who sent a signal tof2.Iff2responds to signals, thenf2also makes
9:278:22617:18:18:71:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:an offer tow1,  whichw1will accept,  hence leavingf1a payoff of 0.  Iff2ignores signals,
9:279:22705:18:18:71:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:then there is still a fifty percent chance thatw1is actuallyf2’s first choice, in which case an
9:280:22800:18:18:71:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer is tendered and accepted, so thatf1again receives 0.  Otherwise,f1receives 1.  Table
9:281:22890:18:18:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1 summarizesf1’s payoffs conditional on receiving a signal from its second ranked worker,
9:282:22979:18:27:71:193:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the strategies off2.
9:283:23003:27:15:141:470:573:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Table 1:Firmf1’s payoffs conditional on receiving a signal from
9:284:23066:15:26:194:324:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:its second ranked worker.
9:285:23091:26:14:231:380:532:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:f1\f2Respond    Ignore
9:286:23113:14:15:231:367:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:Respondxx
9:287:23122:15:37:231:373:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Ignore01/2
9:288:23132:37:17:89:539:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Table 1 shows that strategies of firms are strategic complements.  If a firm responds to
9:289:23220:17:18:72:540:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals, then the other firm is weakly better off from responding to signals as well.  In this
9:290:23314:18:18:72:540:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:example, iff2switches from the action ignore (not making an offer to a second choice worker
9:291:23405:18:18:72:540:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:who has signaled) to the safe action of responding (making an offer to a second choice worker
9:292:23498:18:18:72:467:395:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:who has signaled), thenf1optimally also takes the safe action of responding.
9:293:23574:18:18:89:539:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Turning  to  equilibrium  analysis,  note  that  ifx >0.5  there  is  a  unique  equilibrium  in
9:294:23670:18:18:72:540:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which both firms respond to signals.  Whenx <0.5, that is when the value of the first choice
9:295:23762:18:18:72:540:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worker is much greater than that of the second ranked worker, there exist two equilibria in
9:296:23853:18:18:72:540:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:pure strategies.  In the first, both firms respond to signals (Respond-Respond) and in the
9:297:23943:18:18:72:540:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:second both firm ignore signals (Ignore-Ignore).10Table 2 summarizes welfare properties of
9:298:24033:18:18:72:540:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:these equilibria.  Note that the expected firm and worker payoffs,  as well as the expected
9:299:24124:18:18:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number  of  matches  when  signals  are  ignored  are  the  same  as  when  there  is  no  signaling
9:300:24224:18:18:72:418:251:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:mechanism, since agent actions in these two settings are identical.11
9:301:24293:18:18:89:539:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Whenever there are multiple equilibria (x <0.5), we can rank them in terms of firm wel-
9:302:24380:18:17:72:540:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fare, worker welfare, and the expected number of matches.  Workers and firms are opposed in
9:303:24471:17:16:81:539:198:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:10There is also a mixed strategy equilibrium whenever there are two pure strategy equilibria.  Properties
9:304:24576:16:8:72:483:182:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of this equilibrium coincide with those in the equilibrium where both firms respond to signals.
9:305:24671:8:16:81:539:174:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:11When  both  firms  respond  to  signals,  since  each  firm  has  a  fifty  percent  chance  of  receiving  a  signal
9:306:24790:16:12:72:540:158:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:from  its  first  choice  worker,  half  the  time  this  strategy  yields  payoff  of  one.   Otherwise  a  firm  has  a  1/4
9:307:24916:12:12:72:540:146:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:chance of receiving a signal from its second choice worker only, yielding a payoff ofx.With a 1/4 chance a
9:308:25022:12:12:72:540:134:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:firm receives no signal, in which case it makes an offer to its first choice worker, who will accept with fifty
9:309:25133:12:12:72:540:122:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:percent probability (whenever she is not the first choice worker of the other firm).  Hence,  expected firm
9:310:25240:12:12:72:539:110:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:payoffs are121 +14x+14121 =5+2x8.  Payoffs for workers can similarly be calculated given these outcomes.
9:311:25344:12:12:71:539:98:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Furthermore, when one firm receives all signals (which happens half the time) there is a fifty percent chance
9:312:25453:12:12:71:539:86:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of firms making offers to the same worker, and hence, of only one match occuring, so the expected number
9:313:25557:12:0:71:189:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of matches is141 +342 =74.
10:314:25584:0:14:141:469:709:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Table 2:Firm payoffs, worker payoffs, and number of matches
10:315:25643:14:26:194:395:695:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:when both firms use the same strategy.
