10:317:25732:17:18:120:450:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Respond-Respond(5 + 2x)/83/47/4
10:318:25763:18:39:132:450:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Ignore-Ignore3/4(2 +x)/43/2
10:319:25790:39:18:72:540:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:their preferences over equilibria:  workers prefer the equilibrium in which both firms respond
10:320:25884:18:18:72:540:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to signals while firms prefer the equilibrium in which they both ignore signals.  Intuitively,
10:321:25978:18:18:72:540:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:while one firm may privately gain from responding to a signal,  such an action may nega-
10:322:26066:18:17:72:540:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tively affect the other firm.  The expected number of matches in the equilibrium when both
10:323:26156:17:18:72:540:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms respond to signals is always greater than in the equilibrium when both firms ignore the
10:324:26249:18:18:72:109:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals.
10:325:26257:18:18:89:539:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:These welfare results enable us to study the effects of introducing a signaling mechanism,
10:326:26347:18:18:72:540:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:as outcomes in the offer game without signals are identical to those when both firms ignore
10:327:26438:18:18:72:540:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals  (even  if  the  Ignore-Ignore  equilibrium  does  not  exist).   The  expected  number  of
10:328:26537:18:18:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:matches  and  the  welfare  of  workers  in  the  offer  game  with  signals  in  any  non-babbling
10:329:26636:18:18:72:540:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibrium are greater than in the offer game with no signals.  The welfare of firms changes
10:330:26729:18:18:72:540:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ambiguously with the introduction of a signaling mechanism. We now show that these results
10:331:26819:18:45:72:125:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:generalize.
10:332:26830:45:34:72:380:335:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:3    The Offer Game with No Signals
10:333:26865:34:26:72:232:301:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:3.1    General Notation
10:334:26888:26:18:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this paper we aim for a simple hiring model in which we can highlight the role of agents
10:335:26979:18:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:being able to credibly signal preferences in the presence of congestion.  We have a market
10:336:27069:18:18:72:540:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with a set of firms,  a set of workers,  and a distribution over firm and worker preferences.
10:337:27162:18:18:72:540:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Each  firm  has  the  capacity  to  hire  at  most  one  worker,  and  each  worker  can  fill  at  most
10:338:27266:18:17:72:540:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:one position.  We examine an extreme form of congestion:  each firm may make at most one
10:339:27354:17:18:72:540:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer to hire a worker, where we implicitly assume that workers have applied to all firms.  In
10:340:27448:18:18:72:540:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:theoffer  game  with  no  signals, firms make an offer based on the limited knowledge of the
10:341:27540:18:18:72:539:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:distribution of worker preferences.  In the second setting,the offer game with signals, before
10:342:27634:18:18:71:539:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offers are made, each worker has the opportunity to send one costless signal to a firm, who
10:343:27725:18:18:71:539:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:may use this signal to partially infer worker preferences.  In the web appendix we show that
10:344:27817:18:18:71:539:96:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the main results carry over when firms have multiple positions and workers can send several
10:345:27908:18:0:71:108:78:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals.
11:346:27917:0:18:89:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:LetF={f1,...,fF}be the set of firms, andW={w1,...,wW}be the set of workers,
11:347:27992:18:18:71:539:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with|F|=Fand|W|=W.  We consider markets with at least two firms and two workers.
11:348:28072:18:18:71:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firms and workers have preferences over each other.  For each firmf, let Θfbe the set of
11:349:28160:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:all possible preference lists over workers, whereθf∈Θfis a vector of lengthW.  We use
11:350:28245:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the convention that the worker of rank one is the most preferred worker, while the worker of
11:351:28337:18:18:72:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:rankWis the least preferred worker.  The set of all firm preference profiles is ΘF= (Θf)F.
11:352:28427:18:18:72:539:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Similarly,  we defineθw,  Θwand ΘWfor workers.  Let Θ≡ΘF×ΘW,  and lett(·) be the
11:353:28507:18:18:72:276:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:distribution over preference list profiles.
11:354:28550:18:18:89:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firmfwith preference listθfvalues a match with workerwasu(θf,w),whereu(θf,·)
11:355:28626:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is a von-Neumann Morgenstern utility function.  In our model, firms will be symmetric in
11:356:28714:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the following sense:  we assume that a firm’s utility for a match depends only on a worker’s
11:357:28806:18:18:72:539:510:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:rank.  That is, for any permutationρof worker indices,we haveu(ρ(θf),ρ(w)) =u(θf,w).12
11:358:28892:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Furthermore, all firms have the same utility functionu(·,·).  Workerwwith preference list
11:359:28981:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:θwvalues a match with firmfasv(θw,f),where match utility again depends only on rank,
11:360:29065:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and  all  workers  share  the  same  utility  function.   Though  not  essential  for  our  results,  we
11:361:29169:18:18:72:540:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:will assume that workers and firms derive zero utility from being unmatched, and that any
11:362:29258:18:18:72:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:match is preferable to remaining unmatched for all participants.  Amarketis given by the
11:363:29346:18:18:72:184:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:5-tuple〈F,W,t,u,v〉.
11:364:29365:18:18:89:539:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:For Sections 3-5,  we will focus on a simple preference structure:  each firmfhas pref-
11:365:29452:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:erences over the workers chosen uniformly, randomly and independently from the set of all
11:366:29541:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strict preference orderings over all workers.  Worker preferences are analogously chosen; that
11:367:29635:18:18:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is, there is no correlation in preferences.  This will make the problem symmetric and easy to
11:368:29728:18:18:72:113:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:analyze.
11:369:29736:18:18:89:539:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In Section 6 we will relax this assumption, and consider the case in which preferences of
11:370:29825:18:18:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers over firms may exhibit correlation.  In the web appendix we consider a more involved
11:371:29917:18:39:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:symmetric model where firms have several slots to fill, and workers can send multiple signals.
11:372:30011:39:25:72:341:220:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:3.2    The Offer Game with No Signals
11:373:30048:25:18:72:540:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We first examine behavior in the absence of a signaling mechanism.  Play proceeds as follows.
11:374:30141:18:18:72:540:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:After preferences of firms and workers are realized, each firm simultaneously makes an offer
11:375:30233:18:18:72:540:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to at most one worker.  Workers then choose at most one offer from those available to them.
11:376:30324:18:18:72:540:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Sequential rationality ensures that workers will always select the best available offer.  Hence,
11:377:30420:18:15:81:540:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:12Letρ:{1,...,W} → {1,...,W}be a permutation.  Abusing notation, we applyρto preference lists,
11:378:30514:15:12:72:540:108:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:workers, and sets of workers such that the permutation applies to the worker indices.  For example, suppose
11:379:30621:12:12:72:540:96:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f6:W= 3, ρ(1) = 2, ρ(2) = 3,andρ(3) = 1.  Then we haveθf= (w1,w2,w3)⇒ρ(θf) = (w2,w3,w1) and
11:380:30709:12:0:72:124:84:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f6:ρ(w1) =w2.
12:381:30721:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we take the workers’ behavior in the last stage as given and focus on the reduced game with
12:382:30812:18:18:72:228:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:only firms as strategic players.
12:383:30844:18:18:89:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Once its preference listθf(f’s type) is realized,  firmfdecides whether and to whom
12:384:30927:18:18:72:539:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to make an offer.  Firmfmay use a mixed strategy denoted byσfwhich maps the set of
12:385:31009:18:18:71:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preference lists to the set of distributions over the union of workers with the no-offer option,
12:386:31105:18:18:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:denoted byN; that isσf: Θf→∆(W ∪N).13We denote a profile of all firms’ strategies
12:387:31186:18:18:71:385:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:asσF= (σf1,...σfF), and the set of firmf’s strategies as Σf.
12:388:31246:18:18:89:539:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Let  the  functionπf:  (Σf)F×Θ→Rdenote  the  payoff  of  firmfas  a  function  of
12:389:31327:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firm  strategies  and  realized  agent  types.   We  are  now  ready  to  define  the  Bayesian  Nash
12:390:31428:18:28:72:305:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibrium of the offer game with no signals.
12:391:31474:28:18:72:539:518:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Definition 1.Strategy profile ˆσFis a Bayesian Nash equilibrium in the offer game with no
12:392:31563:18:14:72:540:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals, if for allf∈ Fand ̄θf∈Θfthe strategy ˆσfmaximizes the profit of firmfof type
12:393:31648:14:21:72:122:486:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3: ̄θf, that is
12:394:31661:21:28:184:427:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:ˆσf( ̄θf)∈arg maxσf∈ΣfEθ−f(πf(σf,ˆσ−f,θ)| ̄θf).
12:395:31708:28:18:89:539:437:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  focus  on  equilibria  in  which  firm  strategies  areanonymous;that  is,  they  depend
12:396:31800:18:18:72:540:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:only  on  workers’  ranks  within  a  firm’s  preference  list.   This  rules  out  strategies  that  rely
12:397:31906:18:18:72:540:401:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:on  worker  indices,  eliminating  any  coordination  linked  to  the  identity  of  workers.   As  an
12:398:32008:18:18:72:540:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:example,  “always  make  an  offer  to  my  second-ranked  worker”  is  an  anonymous  strategy,
12:399:32104:18:28:72:379:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:while “always make an offer to the worker calledw2” is not.
12:400:32163:28:18:72:539:337:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Definition  2.Firmf’s  strategyσfisanonymousif  for  any  permutationρ,and  for  any
12:401:32247:18:28:72:368:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:preference profileθf∈Θf, we haveσf(ρ(θf)) =ρ(σf(θf)).
12:402:32300:28:18:89:539:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:When deciding whom to make an offer, firms must consider both the utility from hiring a
12:403:32387:18:18:72:540:273:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:specific worker and the likelihood that this worker will accept an offer. Because preferences of
12:404:32483:18:18:72:540:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:both firms and workers are independently and uniformly chosen from all possible preference
12:405:32573:18:17:72:540:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:orderings, and since firms use anonymous strategies, an offer to any worker will be accepted
12:406:32665:17:18:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with  equal  probability.   Hence,  each  firm  optimally  makes  an  offer  to  the  highest-ranked
12:407:32765:18:18:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worker on its preference list. Indeed, this is the unique equilibrium when firms use anonymous
12:408:32859:18:28:72:124:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategies.
12:409:32870:28:18:72:540:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition 1.The  unique  equilibrium  of  the  offer  game  with  no  signals  when  firms  use
12:410:32967:18:18:72:538:138:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f8:anonymous strategies and workers accept the best available offer isσf(θf) =θ1ffor allf∈F
12:411:33055:18:19:72:137:120:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f9:andθf∈Θf.
12:412:33064:19:10:81:540:101:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:13In other words,fselects elements of aW-dimensional simplex;σf(θf)∈∆W,where ∆W={x∈RW+1:
12:413:33152:10:10:72:101:91:10:g_d0_f19:7:g_d0_f5:∑W+1
12:414:33156:10:0:82:235:81:7:g_d0_f12:10:g_d0_f6:i=1xi= 1, andxi≥0 for eachi}.
13:415:33187:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Note that the above statement requires that firm strategies be anonymous only in equi-
13:416:33273:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:librium.   Firm  deviations  that  do  not  satisfy  the  anonymity  assumption  are  still  allowed.
13:417:33374:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:As seen in the example in Section 2, in this equilibrium there might be considerable lack of
13:418:33466:18:45:72:377:654:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:coordination, leaving many firms and workers unmatched.14
13:419:33523:45:30:72:349:609:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:4    The Offer Game with Signals
13:420:33555:30:18:72:540:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We now modify the game so that each worker may send a “signal” to exactly one firm.  A
13:421:33641:18:18:72:540:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signal is a fixed message;  that is, the only decision of workers is whether and to whom to
13:422:33732:18:18:72:540:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:send a signal.  No decision can be made about the content of the signal.  Note that the signal
13:423:33826:18:18:72:540:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:does not directly affect the utility a firm derives from a worker,  as the firm’s utility from
13:424:33920:18:18:72:540:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:hiring a worker is determined by how high the firm ranks that worker.  However, the signal
13:425:34010:18:18:72:539:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of a worker may affect a firm’s beliefs over whether that worker is likely toacceptan offer.
13:426:34102:18:18:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Since we have a congested market where firms can only make one offer, these beliefs may
13:427:34189:18:18:72:540:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:affect the firm’s decision of whom to make an offer.  The offer game with signals proceeds in
13:428:34282:18:28:72:136:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:three stages:
13:429:34295:28:17:86:540:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.  Agents’ preferences are realized.  Each worker decides whether to send a signal, and to
13:430:34386:17:18:101:540:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which firm.  Signals are sent simultaneously, and are observed only by firms who have
13:431:34471:18:28:101:175:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:received them.
13:432:34485:28:28:86:512:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.  Each firm makes an offer to at most one worker; offers are made simultaneously.
13:433:34568:28:28:86:473:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.  Each worker accepts at most one offer from the set of offers she receives.
13:434:34646:28:18:72:540:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Once again, sequential rationality ensures that workers will always select the best available
13:435:34739:18:18:72:540:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer.   Hence,  we  take  this  behavior  for  workers  as  given  and  focus  on  the  reduced  game
13:436:34841:18:18:72:240:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:consisting of the first two stages.
13:437:34876:18:18:89:539:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In  the  first  stage,  each  worker  sends  a  signal  to  a  firm,  or  else  chooses  not  to  send  a
13:438:34981:18:18:72:539:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signal.  A mixed strategy for workerwis a map from the set of all possible preference lists
13:439:35072:18:18:72:539:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to the set of distributions over the union of firms and the no-signal option, denoted byN;
13:440:35162:18:18:72:540:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that is,σw: Θw→∆(F ∪N).  In the second stage, each firm observes the set of workers
13:441:35245:18:17:72:540:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that sent it a signal,WS⊂W, and based on these signals forms beliefsμf(·|WS) about the
13:442:35331:17:18:72:540:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preferences of workers.  Each firm, based on these beliefs as well as its preferences, decides
13:443:35425:18:18:72:539:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whether and to whom to make an offer.  A mixed strategy of firmfis a map from the set of
13:444:35513:18:19:72:540:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:all possible preference lists, Θf, and the set of all possible combinations of received signals,
13:445:35609:19:16:81:539:90:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:14Note  that our  model of  a  congested  market  is reminiscent of  the  micro-foundations  for  the  matching
13:446:35720:16:0:72:328:74:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:function in the search literature (see e.g. Pissarides, 2000).
14:447:35784:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2W, which is the set of all subsets of workers, to the set of distributions over the union of
14:448:35877:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers and the no-offer option.  That is,σf: Θf×2W→∆(W ∪N).  We denote a profile
14:449:35958:18:18:72:528:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of all worker and firm strategies asσW= (σw1,...σwW) andσF= (σf1,...σfF) respectively.
14:450:36044:18:18:89:539:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The payoff to firmfis a function of firm and worker strategies and realized agent types,
14:451:36132:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:which  we  again  denote  asπf:  (Σw)W×(Σf)F×Θ→R.   Similarly,  define  the  payoff  of
14:452:36219:18:18:72:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers asπw: (Σw)W×(Σf)F×Θ→R.  As the offer game with signals is a multi-stage
14:453:36298:18:28:71:539:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:game of incomplete information, we consider sequential equilibrium as the solution concept.
14:454:36389:28:18:71:540:572:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Definition  3.The  strategy  profile  ˆσ=  (ˆσW,ˆσF)  and  posterior  beliefs  ˆμf(·|WS)  for  each
14:455:36488:18:28:72:453:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firmfand each subset of workersWS⊂Ware a sequential equilibrium if
14:456:36554:28:28:89:490:526:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f9:•for anyw∈W, ̄θw∈ΘW: ˆσw( ̄θw)∈arg maxσw∈ΣwEθ−w(πw(σw,ˆσ−w,θ)| ̄θw),
14:457:36622:28:30:89:282:498:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:•for anyf∈F, ̄θf∈Θf,WS⊂W:
14:458:36647:30:31:101:409:468:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:ˆσf( ̄θf,WS)∈arg maxσf∈ΣfEθ−f(πf(σf,ˆσ−f,θ)| ̄θf,WS,ˆμf),
14:459:36704:31:18:71:539:437:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:where ˆσ−adenotes the strategies of all agents excepta, fora=w,f, and beliefs are defined
14:460:36793:18:28:71:170:419:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:using Bayes’ rule.15
14:461:36813:28:18:89:539:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We again focus on equilibria where agents use anonymous strategies, thereby eliminating
14:462:36900:18:28:71:249:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unrealistic sources of coordination.
14:463:36936:28:18:71:539:345:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Definition 4.Firmf’s strategyσfisanonymousif for any permutationρ, preference profile
14:464:37021:18:18:71:540:327:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:θf∈Θf,and subset of workersWS⊂Wwho sendfa signal, we haveσf(ρ(θf),ρ(WS)) =
14:465:37095:18:18:71:540:309:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:ρ(σf(θf,WS)).Workerw’s strategyσwisanonymousif for any permutationρand preference
14:466:37176:18:39:71:320:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:profileθw∈Θw,we haveσw(ρ(θw)) =ρ(σw(θw)).
14:467:37217:39:25:71:256:252:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4.1    Equilibrium Analysis
14:468:37244:25:18:71:539:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To analyze equilibrium behavior, we first turn to the workers’ choice of whether and to whom
14:469:37336:18:18:71:539:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to send a signal.  In any symmetric equilibrium in which workers send signals and signals
14:470:37425:18:18:71:539:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are interpreted as a sign of interest by firms and hence increase the chance of receiving an
14:471:37517:18:18:71:539:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer,each worker sends her signal to her most preferred firm.  Since sending a signal to any
14:472:37610:18:18:71:539:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firm  will  lead  to  identical  probabilities  of  receiving  an  offer,  it  is  optimal  for  each  worker
14:473:37719:18:18:71:539:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to simply send its signal to its highest ranked firm (see Proposition 4 in Section 6, which
14:474:37810:18:18:71:397:119:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:provides the analog of this statement for a more general setup).
14:475:37874:18:16:81:539:101:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:15As usual in a sequential equilibrium, permissible off-equilibrium beliefs are defined by considering the
14:476:37980:16:0:72:235:85:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:limits of completely mixed strategies.
15:477:38020:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Note that babbling equilibria in which no information is transmitted via signals also exist.
15:478:38112:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In one form of such equilibria, firms ignore signals and workers randomize any signals they
15:479:38203:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:send across firms.  In another version, workers do not send signals, and firms interpret unex-
15:480:38297:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:pected signals negatively.  Note however that equilibria where firms interpret off-equilibrium
15:481:38391:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals negatively fail to survive standard equilibrium refinements (see Section 6 for details).
15:482:38487:18:18:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Finally, “perverse” equilibria, where firms interpret signals negatively, e.g.  as a sign of a
15:483:38581:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:particular lack of interest in such a position, and workers nevertheless send such signals do
15:484:38674:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:not exist.  This is because workers may always opt against sending a signal.  We focus on
15:485:38763:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-babbling equilibria, in which each worker sends a signal only to her most preferred firm.
15:486:38856:18:18:89:539:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Hence, we have pinned down worker equilibrium behavior:  workers send a signal to their
15:487:38943:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:highest ranked firm, and workers accept the best available offer.  We now examine offers of
15:488:39034:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms in the second stage of the game, taking the strategies of workers and beliefs of firms
15:489:39126:18:18:72:259:492:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:about interpreting signals as given.16
15:490:39164:18:17:89:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Callf’s most preferred workerTf(f’s top-ranked worker).  Consider a firmfthat has
15:491:39245:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:received signals from a subset of workersWS⊂ W.  Callf’s most preferred worker in this
15:492:39331:18:18:71:316:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:subsetSf(f’s most preferred signaling worker).
15:493:39377:18:18:89:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Whenever workers signal to their most preferred firm,  and other firms use anonymous
15:494:39461:18:18:71:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategies,f’s offer choice is reduced to a binary decision between making an offer to the
15:495:39551:18:18:71:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:top ranked worker,Tf,  and the most preferred (potentially) lower-ranked worker who has
15:496:39638:18:18:71:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signaled it,Sf.  When the two coincide, that is whenTf=Sf, there is no tradeoff, and firm
15:497:39727:18:18:71:539:349:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:fwill make an offer to this worker.  The expected payoff toffrom making an offer toTfor
15:498:39814:18:18:71:540:331:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:Sf(whichever yields greater payoff) is strictly greater than the payoff from making an offer
15:499:39906:18:18:71:539:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to any other worker.  This follows from the symmetry of worker preferences and strategies
15:500:39995:18:18:71:540:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the anonymity of firm strategies:  for any two workers who sent a signal,f’s expectation
15:501:40087:18:18:71:540:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that these workers will accept an offer is identical.  Hence, iffmakes an offer to a worker
15:502:40178:18:18:71:539:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:who sent a signal, it should make that offer to the worker it prefers the most among them.
15:503:40268:18:17:71:539:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The same logic holds for any two workers who have not sent a signal.  (Propositions A2 and
15:504:40358:17:18:71:461:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A3 in Appendix A.2 provide a rigorous argument for the above statements).
15:505:40431:18:22:89:524:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This suggests a special kind of strategy for firms, which we will call acutoff strategy.
15:506:40519:22:18:71:540:184:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:Definition 5(Cutoff Strategies).Strategyσfis acutoff strategyfor firmfif∃j1,...,jW∈
15:507:40602:18:40:71:504:166:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:{1,...,W},such that for anyθf∈Θfand any setWSof workers who sent a signal,
15:508:40676:40:0:193:262:126:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:σf(θf,WS) =
15:509:40687:0:12:265:275:146:12:g_d0_f19:12:g_d0_f19:{
15:510:40688:12:18:280:411:134:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f18:Sfif rankθf(Sf)≤j|WS|
15:511:40709:18:19:280:358:116:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:Tfotherwise.
15:512:40721:19:15:81:539:97:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:16Note that in any non-babbling symmetric equilibrium, all information sets for firms are realized with
15:513:40824:15:12:72:540:82:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:positive probability.  Hence,  firm beliefs are determined by Bayes’ Law:  if a firm receives a signal from a
15:514:40933:12:0:72:386:70:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:worker, it believes that worker ranks the firm first in her preference list.
16:515:41011:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We call (j1,...,jW)f’scutoff vector, which has as its componentscutoffsfor each positive
16:516:41099:18:28:71:239:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number|WS|of received signals.
16:517:41129:28:18:89:539:662:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A firmfwhich employs a cutoff strategy need only look at the rank of the most preferred
16:518:41216:18:18:71:540:644:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worker who sent it a signal, conditional on the number of signalsfhas received.  If the rank
16:519:41308:18:18:71:539:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of this worker is below a certain cutoff (lower ranks are better since one is the most preferred
16:520:41404:18:18:71:540:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:rank), then the firm makes an offer to this most preferred signaling workerSf.  Otherwise the
16:521:41497:18:18:71:539:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firm makes an offer to its overall top ranked workerTf.  Cutoffs may in general depend on the
16:522:41590:18:18:71:539:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number of signals the firm receives.  This is because the number of signals received provides
16:523:41683:18:18:71:539:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:information about the signals the other firms received.  This in turn affects the behavior of
16:524:41776:18:18:71:540:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firms and hence the optimal decision for firmf.  Note that any cutoff strategy is, by
16:525:41867:18:18:72:248:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:definition, an anonymous strategy.
16:526:41901:18:18:89:539:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:While  we  defined  cutoffs  as  integers,  we  can  extend  the  definition  to  include  all  real
16:527:42001:18:17:72:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:numbers in the range (1,W) by letting a cutoffj+λ,whereλ∈(0,1),correspond to mixing
16:528:42084:17:18:72:473:465:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:between cutoffjand cutoffj+ 1 with probabilities 1−λandλrespectively.17
16:529:42155:18:18:89:539:447:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Cutoff strategies are not only intuitive but alsooptimalstrategies for firms.  Whenever
16:530:42242:18:18:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firms use anonymous strategies and workers signal to their most preferred firms, for
16:531:42332:18:18:72:540:411:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:any strategy of firmfthere exists a cutoff strategy that provides firmfwith a weakly higher
16:532:42423:18:18:72:540:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expected payoff (see Proposition A3).  This is due to the fact that the preferences of firms
16:533:42515:18:18:72:540:375:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and strategies of workers are symmetric.  Consequently, the probability that firmf’s offer
16:534:42605:18:18:72:540:357:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:toTforSfwill be accepted depends only on the number of signals firmfreceives, and not
16:535:42690:18:18:72:539:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:on the identity of the signaling workers.  Hence,  ifffinds it optimal to make an offer to
16:536:42780:18:18:72:539:321:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:Sf, it will certainly make an offer to a more preferredSf, provided the number of signals it
16:537:42872:18:18:72:540:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:receives is the same.  The equilibrium results in this paper will all involve firms using cutoff
16:538:42968:18:18:72:124:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategies.
16:539:42979:18:18:89:539:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Since  cutoff  strategies  can  be  represented  by  cutoff  vectors,  we  can  impose  a  natural
16:540:43077:18:18:72:540:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:partial order on them:  firmf’s cutoff strategyσ′fis greater than cutoff strategyσfif all
16:541:43166:18:17:72:539:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cutoffs ofσ′fare weakly greater than all cutoffs ofσfand at least one of them is strictly
16:542:43255:17:18:72:539:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:greater.  We say that firmfresponds moreto signals than firmf′whenσfis greater than
16:543:43338:18:18:72:89:196:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:σf′.
16:544:43342:18:18:89:539:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  now  examine  how  a  firm  should  adjust  its  behavior  in  response  to  changes  in  the
16:545:43439:18:28:72:540:160:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:behavior of opponents.  We find that responding to signals is a case of strategic complements.
16:546:43533:28:18:72:540:132:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition 2(Strategic Complements).Suppose  workers  send  signals  to  their  most  pre-
16:547:43624:18:18:72:540:114:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:ferred  firms  and  accept  their  best  available  offer,  and  suppose  all  firms  use  cutoff  strategies
16:548:43733:18:15:81:538:96:7:g_d0_f5:7:g_d0_f12:17This is equivalent tofmaking offers toSfwhenSfis ranked better thanj, randomizing betweenTf
16:549:43826:15:0:72:383:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:andSfwhenSfhas rank exactlyj, and making offers toTfotherwise.
17:550:43890:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:and firmfuses a cutoff strategy that is a best response.  If one of the other firms responds
17:551:43982:18:26:72:538:690:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:more to signals, then the best response for firmfis to also weakly respond more to signals.
17:552:44073:26:17:89:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:When other firms make offers to workers who have signaled to them, it is risky for firm
17:553:44160:17:18:72:539:647:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:fto make an offer to a worker who has not signaled to it.  Such a worker has signaled to
17:554:44248:18:18:72:540:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:another firm, which is more inclined to make her an offer.  The greater this inclination on the
17:555:44343:18:18:72:540:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:part of the firm’s opponents, the riskier it is for firmfto make an offer to its most preferred
17:556:44438:18:18:72:539:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:overall workerTf.  Hence as a response, firmfis also more inclined to make an offer to its
17:557:44528:18:18:71:408:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:most preferred worker among those who sent a signal, namelySf.
17:558:44590:18:18:89:539:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The  strategic  complements  result  allows  us  to  apply  Theorem  5  from  Milgrom  and
17:559:44680:18:18:71:539:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Roberts (1990) to demonstrate the existence of symmetric equilibria in pure cutoff strategies
17:560:44773:18:25:71:535:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with smallest and largest cutoffs (see the proof of Theorem 1 in Appendix A.1 for details).
17:561:44864:25:18:71:540:496:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Theorem 1(Equilibrium Existence).In the offer game with signals, there exists a symmetric
17:562:44953:18:18:71:539:478:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:equilibrium in pure cutoff strategies where 1) workers signal to their most preferred firms and
17:563:45048:18:18:71:539:460:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:accept  their  best  available  offer  and  2)  firms  use  symmetric  cutoff  strategies.  Furthermore,
17:564:45152:18:45:71:428:442:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:there exist pure symmetric equilibria with smallest and largest cutoffs.
17:565:45224:45:27:71:539:397:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:5    The Welfare Effects of Introducing a Signaling Mech-
17:566:45281:27:30:101:150:370:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:anism
17:567:45286:30:18:71:539:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We have analyzed the unique equilibrium in the offer game with no signals,  and we have
17:568:45373:18:17:71:539:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:studied symmetric equilibria in markets with a signaling mechanism.  We focused on non-
17:569:45460:17:18:71:539:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:babbling equilibria where firms interpret signals of workers as a sign of interest, and hence
17:570:45553:18:18:71:539:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:each worker sends a signal to her most preferred firm.  In this section we address the effect
17:571:45646:18:18:71:539:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of introducing a signaling mechanism on the market outcome.  We consider three outcome
17:572:45732:18:18:71:539:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:measures:  the  number  of  matches  in  the  market,  the  welfare  of  firms  and  the  welfare  of
17:573:45833:18:18:71:539:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers, where for agent welfare comparisons we consider Pareto ex-ante expected utility as
17:574:45924:18:18:71:138:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:our criterion.
17:575:45938:18:18:89:539:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Our analysis begins with an incremental approach:  we first study the effect of a single
17:576:46026:18:18:71:539:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firm increasing its cutoff, that is, responding more to signals.  We then rank various signaling
17:577:46122:18:18:71:539:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibria in terms of their outcomes.  Finally, we address how the introduction of a signaling
17:578:46217:18:18:71:327:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mechanism impacts the three measures of welfare.
17:579:46265:18:18:89:539:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The expected welfare for a firmfand a workerware captured byπfandπwrespectively,
17:580:46345:18:18:72:540:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whereπf,πw: ΣWw×ΣFf×Θ→R.  Let the functionm: (Σw)W×(Σf)F×Θ→Rdenote
17:581:46411:18:18:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the expected total number of matches in the market as a function of agent strategies and
17:582:46499:18:0:72:405:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:types.  In this section we restrict the analysis to cutoff strategies.
18:583:46571:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Consider  the  offer  game  with  signals,  in  which  workers  send  their  signal  to  their  first
18:584:46672:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:choice firms, and firms interpret these signals as signs of interest.  Fix the strategies of all
18:585:46768:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firms, and assume that one firm changes its strategy to respond more to signals.  How
18:586:46859:18:24:72:456:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:does this affect the number of matches, and the workers and firms welfare?
18:587:46933:24:18:72:539:630:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition 3.Consider  any  strategy  profile  in  which  firms  use  cutoff  strategies,  workers
18:588:47032:18:18:71:539:612:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:send signals to their most preferred firms, and workers accept their best available offer.  Fix
18:589:47127:18:18:71:540:594:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:the strategies of all firms butfasσ−f.  Let firmf’s strategyσ′fdiffer fromσfonly in that
18:590:47215:18:23:72:428:576:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f7:σ′fresponds more to signals, that is, has higher cutoffs thanσf.  Then
18:591:47285:23:27:89:560:553:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f7:•The expected number of matches increases.  That is,Eθ[m(σ′f,σ−f,θ) ]≥Eθ[m(σf,σ−f,θ) ].
18:592:47372:27:18:89:563:526:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:•The expected payoff of each worker increases.  That is, for eachw∈W,Eθ[πw(σ′f,σ−f,θ) ]≥
18:593:47460:18:26:101:197:508:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f7:Eθ[πw(σf,σ−f,θ) ].
18:594:47478:26:18:89:580:482:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:•The expected payoffs of all firms butfdecrease.  That is, for eachf′∈−f,Eθ[πf′(σ′f,σ−f,θ) ]≤
18:595:47571:18:24:101:397:464:12:g_d0_f16:12:g_d0_f7:Eθ[πf′(σf,σ−f,θ) ](negative spillover on opponent firms).
18:596:47628:24:18:89:539:440:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:When at least one firm in−fresponds to signals, that is has a cutoff strictly greater than
18:597:47718:18:28:72:437:422:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:one for some number of received signals, then all inequalities are strict.
18:598:47792:28:18:89:540:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To understand the first result, observe that when firmfswitches its offer from its first
18:599:47880:18:18:72:539:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:choice  workerTfto  its  most  preferred  signaling  workerSf,  it  is  the  other  offers  received
18:600:47980:18:18:72:540:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:by these two workers that determine the impact on the total number of matches.  If both
18:601:48067:18:18:72:540:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers have other offers, or if neither has another offer, the number of matches is unaffected.
18:602:48163:18:17:72:538:322:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f13:Only when exactly one of these two workers has another offer doesf’s switch fromTftoSf
18:603:48249:17:18:72:540:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:affect the number of matches.  However, conditional on exactly one of these having another
18:604:48339:18:18:72:538:287:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f13:offer, it is weakly more likely to beTf, as this worker has signaled to another firm, whileSf
18:605:48432:18:18:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:has not.  Furthermore,Tfisstrictlymore likely thanSfto have another offer when at least
18:606:48519:18:18:72:540:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:one other firm responds to signals.  Hence, making an offer toSfleads to a greater expected
18:607:48610:18:18:72:201:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:total number of matches.
18:608:48634:18:18:89:539:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In addition to creating more matches in expectation, a firm responding more to signals
18:609:48720:18:18:72:540:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unambiguously increases expected worker welfare.  Note that when firmfchanges its offer
18:610:48807:18:18:72:538:179:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f13:fromTftoSf, then workerSfreceives an offer from her first choice firm, while workerTf
18:611:48892:18:18:72:540:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loses an offer from a firm she ranks second or worse.  Hence, when the number of matches is
18:612:48983:18:18:72:540:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unchanged, average worker welfare increases.  Furthermore, it is more likely that the number
18:613:49075:18:18:72:540:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of matches increases rather than decreases, and once more each match ‘gained’ is one where
18:614:49165:18:18:72:540:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a worker receives her first choice firm, while each match ‘lost’ is one where a worker receives
18:615:49260:18:17:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a firm of her second choice or worse.  It follows that in expectation, each worker gains when
18:616:49353:17:0:72:279:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a firm starts responding more to signals.
19:617:49396:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In contrast, a firmfresponding more to signals has a negative effect on the welfare of
19:618:49482:18:18:71:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firms.  When firmfmakes an offer toTf, this offer may be rejected, asTfmay prefer
19:619:49569:18:18:71:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other firms to firmf.  But an offer fromftoSfcreates “stiff” competition for competing
19:620:49655:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms, since this worker will acceptf’s offer with certainty, and offers from other firms will
19:621:49749:18:18:71:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:be rejected.  Additionally,f’s switch fromTftoSfmay only be pivotal for opponent firms
19:622:49835:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:making “risky” offers to their top ranked workers.  Such offers are more likely to be made
19:623:49925:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:toSfthan toTfsince by signaling,Sfhas indicated she prefersf.  Hence,  in addition to
19:624:50010:18:18:72:539:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:creatingstiffercompetition for−f,f’s switch fromTftoSfcreatesmorecompetition for
19:625:50090:18:18:72:461:564:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:−f.  The combination of these two effects gives the negative spillover result.
19:626:50168:18:18:89:539:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We now use the incremental welfare results to compare welfare across equilibria.  The
19:627:50253:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:following corollary states that for all three of our welfare measures, there is a clear ranking
19:628:50348:18:28:72:424:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of any two symmetric equilibria that can be ordered by their cutoffs.
19:629:50417:28:17:72:539:482:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Corollary 1.Consider any two symmetric cutoff strategy equilibria where in one equilibrium
19:630:50507:17:18:72:540:465:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:firms have greater cutoffs (respond more to signals).  Compared to the equilibrium with lower
19:631:50600:18:18:72:540:447:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:cutoffs, in the equilibrium with greater cutoffs we have the following:  (i) the expected number
19:632:50696:18:18:72:540:429:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:of matches is weakly greater, (ii) workers have weakly higher expected payoffs, and (iii) firms
19:633:50791:18:28:72:251:411:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:have weakly lower expected payoffs.
19:634:50826:28:18:89:539:383:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:Corollary 1 states that firms and workers areopposedin their preferences over equilibria.18
19:635:50917:18:18:72:540:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:When multiple symmetric equilibria exist, workers prefer the equilibrium that involves firms
19:636:51009:18:18:72:540:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:responding the most to signals, that is the greatest cutoffs, while firms prefer the equilibrium
19:637:51105:18:18:72:191:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:with the lowest cutoffs.
19:638:51129:18:18:89:539:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We can now address the effect of adding a signaling mechanism to an offer game with
19:639:51212:18:18:72:540:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:no signals.  We will assume that the equilibrium once the signaling mechanism is introduced
19:640:51303:18:18:72:540:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is one of the symmetric non-babbling equilibria.  Using the results above, we can show that
19:641:51394:18:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:introducing a signaling mechanism weakly increases the welfare of workers and the expected
19:642:51484:18:17:72:540:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number of matches.  Furthermore, the inequality is strict if firms respond to signals at all;
19:643:51577:17:18:72:540:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that is, if for at least some number of signals, firms use strategies that call for an offer to a
19:644:51674:18:18:72:540:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worker who signaled,Sf, even when she is not the first choice workerTf.  In contrast, firm
19:645:51764:18:18:72:540:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:welfare cannot be compared.  As the example in Section 2 illustrates, firm welfare may be
19:646:51853:18:18:72:540:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:higher with or without a signaling mechanism.  The following theorem encapsulates these
19:647:51940:18:26:72:109:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:results.
19:648:51948:26:15:81:539:124:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:18Suppose that when we have a class of cutoff strategies that are strategically equivalent, we allow firms to
19:649:52057:15:12:72:539:109:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:only use the lowest one.  For example, when we haveWworkers, a firm withk >1 signals may have cutoffs
19:650:52158:12:12:72:539:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:ofW−k+ 1 andW−k+ 2 that are strategically equivalent:  the firm always makes an offer toSf.  When
19:651:52255:12:0:72:502:85:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:we focus on the lowest strategically equivalent cutoff, then all inequalities of Corollary 1 are strict.
20:652:52361:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Theorem 2(Welfare).Consider any non-babbling symmetric equilibrium of the offer game
20:653:52445:18:18:71:539:690:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:with signals in which for at least some number of signals, firm strategies call for an offer to
20:654:52540:18:18:71:540:672:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:the signaling worker,Sf, even when she is not the first choice workerTf.  Then the following
20:655:52632:18:28:71:182:654:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:three statements hold.
20:656:52654:28:18:88:540:626:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:i.  The  expected  number  of  matches  is  strictly  greater  than  in  the  unique  equilibrium  of
20:657:52755:18:28:101:258:608:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:the offer game with no signals.
20:658:52786:28:18:84:539:580:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:ii.  The expected welfare of workers is strictly greater than in the unique equilibrium of the
20:659:52880:18:28:101:239:562:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:offer game with no signals.
20:660:52907:28:18:81:540:534:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:iii.  The  welfare  of  firms  may  be  greater  or  smaller  than  in  the  unique  equilibrium  of  the
20:661:53012:18:28:101:239:516:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:offer game with no signals.
20:662:53039:28:18:89:539:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:When introducing a signaling mechanism hurts firm welfare, it is because the negative
20:663:53124:18:17:71:539:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:externality outweighs the individual firm benefit from responding to signals.  The theorem
20:664:53214:17:18:71:539:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:discusses the case in which firms respond to at least some degree to signals in equilibrium.
20:665:53306:18:18:71:539:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Note that when there is a symmetric non-babbling equilibrium where firms ignore signals,
20:666:53394:18:18:71:539:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:then this equilibrium is outcome equivalent to a market without a signaling mechanism, so
20:667:53483:18:18:71:539:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that agents are no worse off with the signaling mechanism.  But provided firms respond even
20:668:53574:18:18:71:539:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:minimally  to  signals  in  equilibrium,  with  the  introduction  of  a  signaling  mechanism,  the
20:669:53674:18:45:71:536:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expected number of matches and the expected welfare for workers increase unambiguously.
20:670:53761:45:30:71:251:318:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:6    Block Correlation
20:671:53783:30:18:71:539:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:So  far  we  assumed  that  worker  preferences  are  symmetric,  uniform  and  independent.   In
20:672:53880:18:18:71:539:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-babbling sequential equilibria, this implies that workers send their signal to their most
20:673:53973:18:18:71:539:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preferred  firm,  and  a  firm  that  received  a  signal  could  be  certain  that  an  offer  would  be
20:674:54078:18:18:71:539:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:accepted.  In this section we relax the assumption that worker preferences are uncorrelated.
20:675:54170:18:18:71:539:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:More precisely, we consider a market where firms can be partitioned in blocks, so that all
20:676:54260:18:18:71:539:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers agree which block contains the most desirable firms, which block the second most
20:677:54348:18:18:71:539:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:desirable set of firms and so on.  However, within a block, workers may have idiosyncratic
20:678:54438:18:17:71:539:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preferences over firms.  Hence, for this section we consider markets where agent preferences
20:679:54530:17:28:71:172:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:areblock-correlated.
20:680:54550:28:18:71:540:117:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Definition 6.Ablock-correlated marketis a market〈F,W,t,u,v〉such that for a partition
20:681:54634:18:18:71:539:99:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:F1,...,FBof  the  firms  into  blocks,  ordinal  preferences  (as  encompassed  int(·))  are  such
20:682:54732:18:0:71:92:81:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that
21:683:54738:0:18:86:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.  For anyb < b′, whereb,b′∈ {1,...,B}, each worker prefers every firm in blockFbto
21:684:54822:18:28:101:211:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:any firm in blockFb′;
21:685:54843:28:27:86:521:662:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.  Each worker’s preferences within each blockFbare uniform and independent; and
21:686:54924:27:27:86:442:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.  Each firm’s preferences over workers are uniform and independent.
21:687:54993:27:18:89:540:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  call  distributionst(·)  that  satisfy  the  criteria  in  Definition  6block  uniform.   The
21:688:55090:18:17:72:540:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:environment  analyzed  in  previous  sections  is  a  special  case  of  block-correlated  markets,
21:689:55189:17:18:72:540:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:where there is only one block of firms.  Block-correlated markets are meant to capture the
21:690:55279:18:18:72:540:555:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:notion that many two-sided markets are segmented.  That is, workers may largely agree on
21:691:55367:18:18:72:540:537:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the ranking of blocks on the other side of the market, but vary in their preferences within
21:692:55458:18:18:72:540:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:each block.  For example, workers might agree on the set of firms that constitute the “top
21:693:55548:18:18:72:540:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tier” of the market; however within that tier, preferences are influenced by factors specific
21:694:55641:18:18:72:150:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to each worker.
21:695:55656:18:18:89:539:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We again focus on equilibria where agents use anonymous strategies.  For firms we main-

22:733:58406:31:18:89:539:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Proposition 4 states that there are two types of block-symmetric equilibria that satisfy
22:734:58494:18:18:71:539:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Criterion  D1.   Equilibria  of  the  first  type  are  babbling,  where  firms  ignore  signals.   The
22:735:58597:18:18:71:539:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:outcomes of these equilibria coincide with the outcome in the offer games with no signals.
22:736:58687:18:18:71:410:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Consequently, the signaling mechanism adds no value in this case.
22:737:58752:18:18:89:539:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In equilibria of the second type, workers send signals only to their most preferred firm in

22:748:59696:18:16:81:539:127:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:19Criterion D1 lets us characterize beliefs when firms receive “unexpected,” or off-equilibrium, signals.  See

23:753:60212:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:interprets a signal from a workerwas indicating it is the most preferred firm ofwin that
23:754:60300:18:18:72:539:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:blockbest-in-block  beliefs.   We  will  now  assume  that  workers  use  symmetric  best-in-block
23:755:60398:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategies and that firms have best-in-block beliefs,  and examine firm offers in the second
23:756:60490:18:18:72:173:654:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:stage of the game.20
23:757:60510:18:18:89:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:An important difference between the single block and multi-block settings is that when
23:758:60596:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:there are multiple blocks, offers to workers who have signaled are no longer guaranteed to
23:759:60686:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:be accepted.  This is because a firm that receives a signal knows that while it is the worker’s
23:760:60781:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:most preferred firm in the block, the worker may receive an offer from a firm in a superior
23:761:60872:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:block. Nevertheless, several results about the strategies of firms carry over when we introduce
23:762:60967:18:18:72:539:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:block correlation.  In a block-correlated market, firmf’s offer choice is again reduced to a
23:763:61059:18:18:72:539:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:binary decision betweenTfandSf, provided workers use symmetric best-in-block strategies
23:764:61146:18:18:72:539:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and firms−fuse anonymous strategies.  Under these same conditions, cutoff strategies are
23:765:61234:18:18:71:540:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:again  optimal  forf.   The  strategic  complements  result  of  Proposition  2  also  carries  over;
23:766:61335:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:if  firms−fuse  cutoff  strategies  and  workers  use  symmetric  best-in-block  strategies,  then
23:767:61433:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whenf′∈ −fresponds more to cutoffs,foptimally responds more to cutoffs as well (see
23:768:61516:18:18:72:228:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Propositions A2, A3, and A4).
23:769:61545:18:18:89:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The next result establishes the existence of equilibria in block correlated settings in the
23:770:61636:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer game with signals.  To prove the theorem, we first demonstrate equilibrium existence
23:771:61726:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:while requiring firms to use only cutoff strategies.  We then invoke the optimality of cutoffs
23:772:61820:18:28:72:307:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:result to show that this step is not restrictive.
23:773:61869:28:18:72:544:339:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Theorem 3(Equilibrium Existence under Block Correlation).There exists a block-symmetric
23:774:61956:18:18:72:540:321:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:equilibrium where 1) workers play symmetric best-in-block strategies, and 2) firms play block-
23:775:62050:18:28:72:212:303:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:symmetric cutoff strategies.
23:776:62078:28:18:89:539:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In contrast to Theorem 1 which established equilibrium existence when there is a single
23:777:62165:18:18:72:540:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:block,  equilibria  here  may  involve  mixed  strategies  for  workers;  that  is,  each  worker  may
23:778:62267:18:17:72:330:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signal with positive probability to multiple blocks.
23:779:62319:17:18:89:539:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The final result of the section extends the welfare results of Theorem 2.  Note that for
23:780:62407:18:18:72:540:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the comparisons in the theorem to be strict, we require a block with at least two firms where
23:781:62500:18:18:72:540:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in equilibrium, workers send signals with positive probability to that block.  Without this
23:782:62591:18:28:72:292:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:condition, we only have weak comparisons.
23:783:62632:28:16:81:539:140:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:20Note that firms have best-in-block beliefs on the equilibrium path in any block-symmetric equilibrium.
23:784:62736:16:12:72:540:124:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:In  addition,  a  block-symmetric  equilibrium  satisfies  Criterion  D1  if  and  only  if  worker  strategies  remain
23:785:62855:12:12:72:540:112:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:optimal if firm off-equilibrium beliefs were best-in-block beliefs.  Hence,  we will focus on equilibria where

23:787:63072:12:0:72:137:88:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:A.2 for details.
24:788:63090:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Theorem 4(Welfare under Block Correlation).Consider any non-babbling block-symmetric

24:791:63289:28:18:88:540:644:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:i.  The  expected  number  of  matches  is  strictly  greater  than  in  the  unique  equilibrium  of
24:792:63390:18:28:101:258:626:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:the offer game with no signals.

24:794:63515:18:28:101:239:580:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:offer game with no signals.
24:795:63542:28:18:81:540:552:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:iii.  The  welfare  of  firms  may  be  greater  or  smaller  than  in  the  unique  equilibrium  of  the
24:796:63647:18:28:101:239:534:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:offer game with no signals.
24:797:63674:28:18:89:539:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Note that while the welfare comparisons with and without a signaling mechanism gener-
24:798:63759:18:18:72:540:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:alize to block correlated markets, the welfare comparisons across equilibria (see Corollary 1)
24:799:63853:18:17:72:540:470:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:do not generalize.  In particular, when there are multiple blocks, when a single firm responds
24:800:63947:17:18:72:540:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:more to signals, firms in lower ranked blocks may benefit.  Hence, we no longer see a purely
24:801:64039:18:18:72:539:435:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:negative spillover on other firms, which was a key step in establishing the welfare ranking.21
24:802:64133:18:18:89:539:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:However, even when workers have correlated preferences, so that receiving a signal does
24:803:64220:18:18:71:539:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:not translate to a guaranteed match for a firm, we find that introducing a signaling mecha-
24:804:64311:18:45:71:505:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:nism increases the expected number of matches and the expected welfare of workers.
24:805:64393:45:28:71:543:336:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:7    Market Structure and The Value of a Signaling Mech-
24:806:64449:28:29:101:150:308:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:anism
24:807:64454:29:18:71:539:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this section, we analyze the effects of introducing a signaling mechanism across different

24:809:64638:18:18:71:326:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:due to the introduction of a signaling mechanism.
24:810:64687:18:18:89:539:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To isolate the impact of a signaling mechanism on the number of matches in the market,
24:811:64773:18:18:71:539:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we consider a special case where agents want to match, but are nearly indifferent over whom
24:812:64864:18:18:71:540:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:they  match  with.   That  is,  firms  (and  workers)  play  an  (almost)pure  coordinationgame

24:814:65050:18:18:72:539:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:partner  as  beingalmostthe  same  across  partners.   If  agentahas  a  preference  profileθa,
24:815:65145:18:0:72:454:135:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f13:agentaprefers to be matched with partnerθka,rather than with partnerθk
24:816:65215:0:10:455:457:142:6:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f17:′

24:818:65219:0:23:472:540:140:8:g_d0_f18:12:g_d0_f3:′> k, though
24:819:65231:23:16:81:539:117:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:21Since offers to workers who have signaled are no longer guaranteed to be accepted, firms making offers
24:820:65335:16:12:72:540:101:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f20:to signaling workers may be affected byf’s switch fromTftoSf.  In particular, firms in thesame or higher

24:822:65547:12:0:71:540:77:10:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f6:fswitch fromTftoSf.  There is a positive spillover on these firms, and negative spillover on all other firms.
25:823:65658:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the difference between utility intensities is very small.22In addition, there is only one block
25:824:65753:18:18:72:389:690:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:of firms, so that agent preferences are uniformly distributed.23
25:825:65817:18:18:89:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Under these assumptions, there is a unique non-babbling symmetric equilibrium in the
25:826:65901:18:18:71:539:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer game with signals.  Each worker sends a signal to her most preferred firm.  Each firm
25:827:65992:18:18:71:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:makes an offer to its most preferred worker that has signaled provided the firm receives at
25:828:66083:18:18:71:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:least one signal; otherwise, it makes an offer to its top-ranked worker (see Proposition B1).24
25:829:66178:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Proposition 1 also applies in this setting; that is, there is a unique equilibrium of the offer
25:830:66273:18:18:72:183:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:game with no signals.
25:831:66294:18:18:89:539:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We denote the expected number of matches in the unique equilibrium in the pure coor-
25:832:66378:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:dination model with signals and withFfirms andWworkers asmS(F,W), and without a
25:833:66457:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signaling mechanism asmNS(F,W).  The increase in expected number of matches from the
25:834:66541:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:introduction of the signaling mechanism, which we term thevalue  of  the  signaling  mecha-
25:835:66632:18:18:72:538:492:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f9:nism, we denote asV(F,W)≡mS(F,W)−mNS(F,W).  Figure 1 graphs 100·V(F,W)/W
25:836:66704:18:17:71:539:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:as a function ofFfor fixedW= 10 andW= 100,and 100·V(F,W)/Fas a function of
25:837:66778:17:18:71:540:457:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:Wfor fixedF= 10 andF= 100.  That is, the figure depicts the increase in the expected
25:838:66862:18:18:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number of matches proportional to the size of the side of the market we keep fixed (which
25:839:66951:18:18:71:405:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:places an upper bound on the total number of possible matches).
25:840:67014:18:18:89:539:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The figures suggest that the value of a signaling mechanism is single peaked when varying
25:841:67103:18:18:71:539:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:one side of the market and holding the other constant.  That is, it seems that a signaling
25:842:67193:18:18:71:539:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mechanism is most beneficial for balanced markets — markets where the the number of firms
25:843:67282:18:18:71:539:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and the number of workers are roughly of the same magnitude.  To understand why signaling
25:844:67371:18:18:71:539:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:may be useful in balanced markets, it is helpful to think about the endpoints.  With many
25:845:67460:18:18:71:539:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers and very few firms, firms will almost certainly match with or without the signaling
25:846:67551:18:21:71:539:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mechanism, as there is no large coordination problem.  With many firms and few workers,
25:847:67638:21:7:81:367:274:7:g_d0_f5:7:g_d0_f12:22The “nearly indifferent” condition for firms is thatu(W)>W
25:848:67698:7:0:361:366:267:7:g_d0_f12:7:g_d0_f12:F
25:849:67699:0:11:371:377:282:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f19:(
25:850:67700:11:0:377:393:271:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f8:1−
25:851:67702:0:8:395:400:279:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f19:(
25:852:67703:8:0:399:424:271:10:g_d0_f6:7:g_d0_f12:1−1W
25:853:67707:0:8:427:444:279:10:g_d0_f19:10:g_d0_f19:)F)
25:854:67710:8:15:446:540:271:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f6:u(1),  whereu(1) and
25:855:67730:15:12:71:540:256:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f6:u(W) are firm utility from matching with first and last ranked workers, respectively.  A complete specification
25:856:67841:12:9:71:261:244:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:of the setup can be found in Appendix B.2.
25:857:67883:9:15:81:539:235:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:23Our pure coordination model has similarities to the “urn-ball” model in the labor literature, concisely
25:858:67988:15:12:71:539:220:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:described in a survey by Petrongolo and Pissarides (2001):  “Firms play the role of urns and workers play the
25:859:68097:12:12:71:539:208:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:role of balls.  An urn becomes “productive” when it has ball in it.  [. . . ]  In the simplest version of this process
25:860:68215:12:12:71:540:196:10:g_d0_f11:10:g_d0_f6:Uworkers know exactly the location ofVjob vacancies and send one application each.  If a vacancy receives
25:861:68320:12:12:71:539:184:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:one or more applications it selects an applicant at random and forms a match.  The other applicants are
25:862:68423:12:12:71:539:172:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:returned to the pool of unemployed workers to apply again.” Our pure coordination model effectively flips
25:863:68528:12:12:71:539:160:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the urn-ball problem around.  Workers apply to all jobs, and firms propose the offers.  We have a non-random
25:864:68636:12:12:71:539:148:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:selection procedure, and of course in our model we study the role of signaling.  Perhaps the paper with the
25:865:68743:12:8:71:364:136:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:closest market structure to ours is Julien, Kennes and King (2000).
25:866:68810:8:16:81:539:128:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:24In  this  case,  one  can  view  the  offer  game  with  no  signals  as  the  result  of  the  first  round  of  a  firm-
25:867:68934:16:12:71:539:112:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:proposing deferred acceptance algorithm.  When workers send signals, the result resembles one round of a
25:868:69038:12:12:71:539:100:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:worker-proposing deferred acceptance with one exception:  firms who received no offer (no signal from any
25:869:69143:12:0:71:212:88:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:worker) do get to make an offer.
