26:910:69407:103:14:141:470:495:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Figure 1:Balanced Markets:  The proportional increase in the
26:911:69467:14:15:200:470:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number of matches due to a signaling mechanism as
26:912:69516:15:14:200:470:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we  vary  the  number  of  firms  for  a  fixed  number  of
26:913:69575:14:36:200:461:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers (left graphs) and vice versa (right graphs).
26:914:69627:36:18:72:540:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the  reverse  holds:  most  workers  will  get  offers  with  or  without  the  signaling  mechanism.
26:915:69728:18:18:72:540:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Hence, the signaling mechanism offers little benefit at the extremes.  Furthermore, Figure 1
26:916:69820:18:18:72:540:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:suggests that the proportional increase in the expected number of matches remains steady as
26:917:69911:18:17:72:540:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:market size increases, holding constant the ratio of workers to firms.  Proposition 5 describes
26:918:70006:17:28:72:215:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:these observations precisely.
26:919:70035:28:18:72:539:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition 5(Balanced Markets).Consider markets with F firms and W workers.  Then
26:920:70117:18:18:72:539:299:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f8:(i)  for  fixedW,V(F,W)attains  its  maximum  value  atF=x0W+OW(1),  wherex0≈
26:921:70194:18:17:72:540:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:1.01211and  (ii)  for  fixedF,V(F,W)attains  its  maximum  value  atW=y0F+OF(1),
26:922:70274:17:28:72:167:264:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:wherey0≈1.8442.
26:923:70289:28:18:89:540:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The proof of Proposition 5 involves the calculation of an explicit formula forV(F,W).
26:924:70374:18:34:72:434:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The expected increase in the number of matches can be represented as
26:925:70442:34:0:232:305:184:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:V(F,W) =α(
26:926:70452:0:16:306:317:192:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:W
26:927:70453:16:0:307:315:176:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:F
26:928:70454:0:33:320:379:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:)F+OF(1)
26:929:70462:33:18:72:97:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:or as
26:930:70467:18:0:228:300:133:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:V(F,W) =β(
26:931:70477:0:16:303:311:141:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:F
26:932:70478:16:0:301:312:125:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:W
26:933:70479:0:26:315:383:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:)W+OW(1),
26:934:70488:26:18:72:539:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whereα(·) andβ(·) are particular functions andOW(1) andOF(1) denote functions that
26:935:70570:18:17:72:539:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are  smaller  than  a  constant  for  largeWand  for  largeFrespectively.   Hence,V(F,W)  is
26:936:70662:17:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:“almost” homogeneous of degree one for large markets.  That is, the proportional increase
27:937:70753:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in the number of matches,V(F,W)/WandV(F,W)/F,  is almost homogenous of degree
27:938:70830:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:zero.25As a consequence, we can evaluate the introduction of the signaling mechanism for a
27:939:70920:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sample market, and its properties will be preserved for markets of other sizes, but with the
27:940:71012:18:18:72:228:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:same ratio of firms to workers.
27:941:71043:18:18:89:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:For  example,  we  can  use  Figure  1  to  investigate  maximal  quantitative  gains  from  the
27:942:71139:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:introduction of the signaling mechanism in large markets.  For a fixed number of workers,
27:943:71228:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the maximum increase in expected number of matches is approximately 15%.  Furthermore,
27:944:71314:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the returns to the signaling mechanism are substantial over a wide range of market conditions.
27:945:71408:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:For example, only when the number of firms outweighs the number of workers by more than
27:946:71495:18:45:72:495:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fourfold do the gains from introducing the signaling mechanism drop to below 1%.
27:947:71575:45:30:72:326:501:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:8    Discussion and Conclusion
27:948:71605:30:18:72:540:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Excessive applications by job market candidates lead to market congestion:  employers must
27:949:71695:18:18:72:540:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:devote resources to evaluate and pursue potential candidates, but cannot give due attention
27:950:71786:18:18:72:540:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to all.  Evaluation is further complicated because employers must assess which applicants,
27:951:71876:18:17:72:525:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:many of whom are performing broad searches, are likely to ultimately accept a job offer.
27:952:71964:17:18:89:539:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Consequently,  applicants are  often  eager  to convey  information  about  their  interest  in
27:953:72059:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:particular employers, and employers stand ready to act upon such information, if it can be
27:954:72149:18:18:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:deemed credible.  However, in many markets indicating preferences is cheap, and employers
27:955:72238:18:18:72:540:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:may struggle to identify which preference information is sincere.  This, in turn, may prevent
27:956:72331:18:18:72:407:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:any potential gains from preference signaling from being realized.
27:957:72397:18:18:89:539:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this paper we examined how a signaling mechanism can overcome this credibility prob-
27:958:72484:18:18:72:540:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:lem and improve agent welfare.  In our model, workers are allowed to send a costless signal
27:959:72575:18:18:72:540:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to a single firm.  While participation is free and voluntary, this mechanism nevertheless pro-
27:960:72669:18:18:72:540:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:vides workers with a means of credibly expressing preferences.  In a symmetric setting where
27:961:72761:18:18:72:540:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:agent preferences are uncorrelated, workers will send their signal to their most preferred firm.
27:962:72857:18:18:72:540:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Firms use this information as guidance, optimally using cutoff strategies to make offers.  We
27:963:72950:18:18:72:540:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:find that on average, introducing a signaling technology increases both the expected number
27:964:73041:18:18:72:540:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of matches as well as the expected welfare of workers.  The welfare of firms,  on the other
27:965:73132:18:17:72:540:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:hand, changes ambiguously, because firms responding more to signals may impose a negative
27:966:73221:17:18:72:540:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:externality on other firms.  The results carry over when we consider a model where firms
27:967:73309:18:18:72:380:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:have many positions, and workers can send multiple signals.
27:968:73368:18:16:81:539:113:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:25Note that this result corroborates the stylized fact in the empirical labor literature that the matching
27:969:73474:16:12:72:540:97:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:function (the expected number of matches) has a constant return to scale.  See, for example, Petrongolo and
27:970:73581:12:0:72:325:85:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:Pissarides (2001) or Rogerson, Shimer and Wright (2005).
28:971:73639:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We showed that the results hold even when workers have correlated preferences, where
28:972:73723:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers  agree  on  the  ranking  of  blocks  of  firms  but  vary  in  their  preferences  within  each
28:973:73827:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:block.  In this case firm offers to workers who have signaled will not result in guaranteed
28:974:73918:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:acceptance.  This is because workers will no longer send their signal to their most preferred
28:975:74011:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firm, but rather will mix among the most preferred firms from each block.  We showed further
28:976:74103:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that introducing a signaling mechanism adds the most value for balanced markets, that is,
28:977:74192:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:markets in which the number of firms and the number of workers are of roughly the same
28:978:74278:18:18:72:129:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:magnitude.
28:979:74288:18:18:89:539:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:One path for future research would be to characterize the full set of agent preferences
28:980:74375:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:where signaling is beneficial.  While in this paper we find that signaling mechanisms can im-
28:981:74468:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:prove agent welfare under a broad class of preferences, for some agent preferences signaling
28:982:74560:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:can worsen outcomes.  Kushnir (2009) models a high-information setting with minimal con-
28:983:74648:18:18:72:540:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:gestion where signals disturb firms’ commonly held beliefs about workers preferences, which
28:984:74739:18:17:72:540:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in turn disrupts the maximal matching.  Kushnir’s example corroborates the intuition that
28:985:74828:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals may be more useful in low information settings than in high.  Further investigation
28:986:74919:18:18:72:241:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of this question could be fruitful.
28:987:74954:18:18:89:539:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Another interesting question that is beyond the scope of the current paper concerns the
28:988:75041:18:18:72:540:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:optimal  signaling  mechanism.   Providing  candidates  with  one,  or  else  a  small  number  of
28:989:75139:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:identical signals offers a tractable approach, and participants may value its simplicity.  But
28:990:75233:18:18:72:540:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:within the realm of mechanisms that offer candidates equal numbers of identical signals, how
28:991:75325:18:18:72:540:349:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:do we identify the optimal number of signals,  especially in light of the fact that multiple
28:992:75417:18:18:72:336:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilbria may exist?  And might we do even better?
28:993:75467:18:18:89:539:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:If we expand the class of mechanisms under study,  we can potentially improve perfor-
28:994:75552:18:18:72:540:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mance  even  more.   For  example,  the  signaling  mechanism  that  maximizes  the  number  of
28:995:75647:18:18:72:540:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:matches may be asymmetric.  Consider the example in Section 2, with two firms and two
28:996:75732:18:18:72:540:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers.   In  the  example,  each  worker  had  exactly  one  signal.   If  both  workers  have  and
28:997:75833:18:17:72:540:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:send two signals that are identical, outcomes are as if each had no signal.  If we offered each
28:998:75928:17:18:72:540:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:worker two distinct signals, e.g.  a ‘gold’ and a ‘silver’ signal, analysis is as if they had one
28:999:76025:18:18:72:131:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signal each.
28:1000:76037:18:18:89:539:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Asymmetric signaling capacities, however, can generate a full matching.  Suppose that
28:1001:76122:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:one worker has a gold signal, while the other has two silver signals.  Suppose further that
28:1002:76213:18:18:72:540:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms are indifferent between the two workers.  Then one equilibrium involves the first worker
28:1003:76307:18:18:72:540:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sending its gold signal to its preferred firm.  The firm that receives the gold signal will make
28:1004:76403:18:18:72:540:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the signaling worker an offer, while the firm who receives no gold signal will make an offer
28:1005:76495:18:18:72:518:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to the worker who sent a silver signal.  Both firms and workers will always be matched.
28:1006:76582:18:0:89:539:80:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The  question  of  the  optimal  signaling  mechanism,  as  well  as  the  question  of  how  the
29:1007:76681:0:18:72:540:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:benefit from signaling varies across market structures,  provide interesting areas for future
29:1008:76774:18:18:72:117:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:research.
29:1009:76783:18:18:89:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We wish to highlight that a signaling mechanism has the potential to improve outcomes
29:1010:76868:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in congested markets.  Importantly, since signaling mechanisms are free, voluntary, and built
29:1011:76961:18:18:72:540:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:on  top  of  existing  labor  markets,  these  improvements  come  in  a  reasonably  non-invasive
29:1012:77059:18:18:72:540:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:manner.  As opposed to a central clearinghouse, as in the National Resident Matching Pro-
29:1013:77148:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:gram (c. f. Roth,  1984 and Roth and Peranson,  1999),  a centralized signaling mechanism
29:1014:77237:18:18:72:540:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requires significantly less intervention.  Market designers may find it easier to get consensus
29:1015:77332:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from  participants  to  introduce  such  a  mechanism,  which  nevertheless  can  offer  significant
29:1016:77432:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:benefits.  As such, we hope that in addition to furthering our understanding of how labor
29:1017:77521:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:markets work, our paper adds to the practical literature that aims at changing and improving
29:1018:77613:18:45:72:159:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:existing markets.
29:1019:77630:45:34:72:189:465:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:A    Appendix
29:1020:77643:34:25:72:368:431:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:A.1    Markets with a single block of firms
29:1021:77686:25:18:72:540:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This portion of the appendix covers proofs for Sections 3-5.  In this setup workers may send
29:1022:77778:18:18:72:540:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:at most one signal, and there is a single block of firms.  We omit proofs of Propositions 1
29:1023:77869:18:18:72:540:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and 2 and Theorem 2 as these are special cases of Propositions A1 and A4 and Theorem 4
29:1024:77955:18:30:72:134:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:respectively.
29:1025:77968:30:17:72:540:322:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Proof of Theorem 1.As discussed in Section 4, in any symmetric non-babbling equilibrium
29:1026:78055:17:18:72:540:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:each worker sends its signal to its most preferred firm.  Consequently, all information sets
29:1027:78147:18:18:72:540:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for firms are realized with positive probability, so firm beliefs are determined by Bayes’ Law:
29:1028:78242:18:18:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:if a firm receives a signal from a worker, it believes that worker ranks the firm first in its
29:1029:78336:18:18:72:540:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:preference list.  We now take these worker strategies and firm beliefs as fixed, and analyze
29:1030:78428:18:18:72:540:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the second stage of the game when firms choose offers.  We will show that this reduced game
29:1031:78519:18:18:72:540:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is a supermodular game, and then use the results of Milgrom and Roberts (1990) to prove
29:1032:78606:18:18:72:138:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:our theorem.
29:1033:78618:18:18:89:539:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We analyze the game where we restrict firm strategies to be cutoff strategies.  Denote
29:1034:78704:18:18:72:540:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the set of cutoff strategy profiles as Σcut, with typical elementσ= (σ1,...,σF).  Recall that
29:1035:78797:18:18:72:540:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a cutoff strategy for firmfis a vectorσf= (j1f,...,jWf) wherejkfcorresponds to the cutoff
29:1036:78886:18:18:71:539:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:when firmfreceivesksignals.  We will consider only strategies where each cutoff is a natural
29:1037:78978:18:18:71:540:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:number, i.e.jkf∈{1,...,W}.  As defined on p.15, vector comparison yields a natural partial
29:1038:79068:18:0:71:303:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:order on Σcut:σ≥Σcutσ′⇔σf≥σ′f⇔jkf≥
29:1039:79102:0:10:307:312:99:12:g_d0_f19:12:g_d0_f19:(
29:1040:79103:10:0:312:321:89:12:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f13:jkf
29:1041:79106:0:10:323:330:99:12:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f18:)′
29:1042:79108:10:18:335:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for anyf∈ Fandk∈ {1,...,W}.  This
29:1043:79141:18:0:71:354:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:partial order is reflexive, antisymmetric, and transitive.
30:1044:79201:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To show that the second stage is a game with strategic complementarities, we need to
30:1045:79285:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:verify thatEθ(πf(σf,σ−f,θ)) is supermodular inσf, and thatEθ(πf(σf,σ−f,θ)) has increas-
30:1046:79372:18:18:72:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ing differences inσfandσ−f.  The former is trivially true because whenfshifts of one its
30:1047:79460:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cutoff vector components, thisdoes not influence the change in payoff from a shift of another
30:1048:79553:18:18:72:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:cutoff vector component.  Namely, if we considerσ1f= (...,jl,...,jk,...), σ2f= (...,j′l,...,jk,...),
30:1049:79653:18:33:72:476:618:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:σ3f= (...,jl,...,j′k,...), andσ4f= (...,j′l,...,j′k,...) for somel,k∈{1,...,W},then
30:1050:79736:33:33:100:511:585:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:Eθ(πf(σ1f,σ−f,θ))−Eθ(πf(σ2f,σ−f,θ)) =Eθ(πf(σ3f,σ−f,θ))−Eθ(πf(σ4f,σ−f,θ)).
30:1051:79809:33:18:89:539:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ThatEθ(πf(σf,σ−f,θ)) has increasing differences inσfandσ−ffollows from Proposition
30:1052:79891:18:32:72:497:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.  Namely, for anyσf, σ−f, σ′f, andσ′−fsuch thatσ′f≥σfandσ′−f≥σ−fwe have
30:1053:79964:32:33:100:511:502:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:Eθ(πf(σ′f,σ′−f,θ))−Eθ(πf(σf,σ′−f,θ))≥Eθ(πf(σ′f,σ−f,θ))−Eθ(πf(σf,σ−f,θ)).
30:1054:80036:33:18:72:540:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Hence  the  second  stage  of  the  game,  when  firms  choose  their  strategies,  is  a  game  with
30:1055:80137:18:18:72:540:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategic  complementarities.   Since  in  our  model  firms  are  ex-ante  symmetric,  Theorem  5
30:1056:80235:18:18:72:540:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of Milgrom and Roberts (1990) establishes the existence of largest and smallest symmetric
30:1057:80324:18:28:72:539:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f25:pure strategy equilibria.-
30:1058:80350:28:18:75:539:387:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Proof of Proposition 3.  The first two results, increase in the expected number of matches
30:1059:80440:18:18:72:540:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and positive spillover on workers, are demonstrated in the proof of Theorem 4 in Section 6
30:1060:80530:18:18:72:540:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(which considers a more general assumption on agent preferences). To avoid repetition, we do
30:1061:80622:18:18:72:540:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:not present the proofs here.  However, the third result, that responding to signals generates
30:1062:80715:18:18:72:540:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a  negative  spillover  on  opponent  firms,  is  unique  to  the  case  when  agent  preferences  are
30:1063:80817:18:18:72:344:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:uniformly distributed, so we present the proof below.
30:1064:80870:18:18:89:539:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Let  firmfstrategyσfdiffer  fromσ′fin  thatσ′fhas  weakly  greater  cutoffs.   Consider
30:1065:80957:18:18:72:539:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:some firmf′∈−f.  For each preference listθf′and set of signals receivedWS, firmf′either
30:1066:81044:18:18:72:538:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:makes an offer toSf′(θf′,WS) orTf′(θf′,WS).  Observe that a change in strategy of firmf
30:1067:81131:18:18:72:539:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:does not affectf′’s payoff from makingSf′an offer.  This follows since each worker sends
30:1068:81219:18:17:72:540:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:her  signal  to  her  most  preferred  firm,  so  offers  to  signaling  workers  are  always  accepted.
30:1069:81323:17:18:72:540:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:However, as shown in the proof of Proposition 2, the probability thatTf′accepts firmf′’s
30:1070:81411:18:18:72:540:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer weakly decreases.  Hence, overall the expected payoff of firmf′∈−fweakly decreases
30:1071:81499:18:29:72:539:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f25:when firmfresponds more to signals:Eθ(πf′(σf,σ−f,θ))≥Eθ(πf′(σ′f,σ−f,θ)).-
30:1072:81572:29:18:76:539:125:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Proof of Corollary 1.That the expected number of matches and the expected welfare of
30:1073:81656:18:18:72:540:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers are higher in the equilibrium with higher cutoffs is a straightforward consequence of
30:1074:81749:18:17:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:iterated application of the first and the second parts of Proposition 3.  In order to show that
30:1075:81844:17:0:72:540:72:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms have lower expected payoffs in the equilibrium with greater cutoffs,  we combine the
31:1076:81936:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:third result of Proposition 3 with a simple equilibrium property.Consider two symmetric
31:1077:82023:18:18:72:539:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibria,  where  firms  play  cutoff  strategiesσandσ′,  withσ′≥σ.   From  the  definition
31:1078:82116:18:18:72:540:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of an equilibrium strategy we haveEθ[πf(σf,σ−f,θ)]≥Eθ[πf(σ′f,σ−f,θ)].The third result
31:1079:82201:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of Proposition 3 yieldsEθ[πf(σ′f,σ−f,θ)]≥Eθ[πf(σ′f,σ′−f,θ)].Combining these inequalities
31:1080:82289:18:39:72:539:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f25:yieldsEθ[πf(σf,σ−f,θ)]≥Eθ[πf(σ′f,σ′−f,θ)].-
31:1081:82332:39:26:72:371:597:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:A.2    General block-correlated preferences
31:1082:82375:26:18:72:540:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This  portion  of  the  the  appendix  covers  proofs  for  Section  6.   In  this  setup  workers  may
31:1083:82478:18:18:72:540:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:send  at  most  one  signal,  and  worker  preferences  are  block-correlated.   We  also  introduce

31:1086:82691:39:18:72:540:478:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition A1(Equilibrium with no signals).The  unique  equilibrium  of  the  offer  game

31:1089:82921:44:18:72:539:398:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition A2(Binary nature of optimal firm offer).Suppose  firms−fuse  anonymous
31:1090:83003:18:18:72:540:380:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:strategies and workers use symmetric best-in-block strategies.  Consider a firmfthat receives
31:1091:83096:18:18:72:538:362:12:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f13:signals  from  workersWS⊂ W.  Then  the  expected  payoff  toffrom  making  an  offer  toSf
31:1092:83187:18:18:71:539:344:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:is  strictly  greater  than  the  payoff  from  making  an  offer  to  any  other  worker  inWS.   The
31:1093:83289:18:18:71:540:326:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:expected payoff to firmffrom making an offer toTfis strictly greater than the payoff from
31:1094:83378:18:44:71:349:308:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:making an offer to any other worker from setW/WS.
31:1095:83427:44:18:71:540:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Proposition A3(Optimality of cutoff strategies).Suppose workers use symmetricbest-in-
31:1096:83512:18:17:71:539:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:blockstrategies and firms have best-in-block beliefs.  Then for any strategyσfof firmf, there
31:1097:83605:17:18:71:539:229:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:exists a cutoff strategy that providesfwith a weakly higher expected payoff thanσffor any
31:1098:83694:18:44:71:321:211:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:anonymous strategiesσ−fof opponent firms−f.
31:1099:83737:44:18:71:540:167:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition  A4(Strategic  complements  under  block  correlation).Suppose  workers  play
31:1100:83826:18:18:71:538:149:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f9:symmetric  best-in-block  strategies,  and  firms−fuse  cutoff  strategies.    If  firmf′∈ −f
31:1101:83919:18:18:71:539:131:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:increases its cutoffs (responds more to signals), firmfwill also optimally weakly increase its
31:1102:84013:18:0:71:108:113:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:cutoffs.
32:1103:84023:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Proof of Proposition 4.We first define an analog of criterionD1 of Cho and Kreps for
32:1104:84107:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:our setting.26Consider some block-symmetric sequential equilibrium.  Fix strategies of all
32:1105:84197:18:18:71:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:agents except workerwand firmf,which we denote asσ−f,w.  Fix also the beliefs of firms
32:1106:84283:18:18:71:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:other  than  firmf,  which  we  denote  asμ−f.   We  now  analyze  strategies  of  workerwand
32:1107:84376:18:18:71:235:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategies and beliefs for firmf.
32:1108:84409:18:18:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:There are two cases where information sets for firms might be reached with zero prob-
32:1109:84494:18:18:71:539:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ability (lie “off the equilibrium path”) in a block-symmetric equilibrium.  First,  when the
32:1110:84586:18:18:71:539:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:symmetric worker equilibrium strategy prescribes zero probability of sending a signal to a
32:1111:84676:18:18:71:539:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:particular block, firms in these blocks would view signals from such workers as “unexpected.”
32:1112:84769:18:18:71:539:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Second, when a firm anticipates receiving a signal with 100% probability, thennotreceiving
32:1113:84859:18:18:71:539:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a  signal  would  correspond  to  an  off-equilibrium  information  set.   But  by  the  anonymous
32:1114:84957:18:18:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategies  assumption,  this  can  only  happen  in  a  block-symmetric  equilibrium  if  the  firm

37:1305:97383:39:18:89:539:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Let us denote firm strategies in the unique equilibrium of the offer game with no signals

37:1308:97661:18:18:71:539:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:matches and the welfare of workers equal the corresponding parameters in the offer game

37:1310:97840:18:18:71:540:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:welfare of workers in a block-symmetric equilibrium in the offer game with signals areweakly

37:1312:98022:18:18:71:414:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:no signals is a consequence of sequential application of Lemma A1.

44:1508:109950:24:18:71:540:532:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Proof of Proposition A3(Optimality of Cutoff Strategies).If workers use best-in-block

50:1783:121969:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:As a corollary ofI)andII), if firmf′increases its cutoff point for some set of signals,

57:2224:134455:39:26:72:540:651:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:B.3    Extension:  Signaling with Many Positions and Many Signals
57:2225:134520:26:18:72:540:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this section we consider a model of matching markets in a symmetric environment that is
57:2226:134610:18:17:72:540:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:similar to the one in Sections 3 and 4.  The difference is that each firm now has the capacity
57:2227:134704:17:18:72:540:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to hire up toLworkers, and each worker may send up toKidentical costless private signals.
57:2228:134793:18:18:71:539:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We  assume  that  the  number  of  signals  each  worker  may  send  is  less  than  the  number  of
57:2229:134893:18:18:71:481:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms,K < F,and each worker can send at most one signal to a particular firm.
57:2230:134970:18:18:89:540:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We assume that firm utilities are additive, i.e.  firmfwith preferencesθfover individual
57:2231:135058:18:0:71:452:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers values a match with a subset of workersW0⊂Wasu(θf,W0) =

57:2235:135225:18:18:71:540:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:listθwvalues a match with firmfasv(θw,f).We keep all assumptions of Sections 3 and 4
57:2236:135309:18:18:71:282:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:regarding agent utilitiesu(·,·) andv(·,·).
57:2237:135351:18:18:89:539:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The  timing  and  strategies  of  agents  of  the  offer  game  without  signals  can  be  adopted
57:2238:135449:18:26:72:150:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:from Section 3:
57:2239:135464:26:17:86:540:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.  Agents’ preferences are realized.  In the case of a signaling mechanism,  each  worker
57:2240:135554:17:18:101:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sends up toKprivate, identical, costless signals to firms.  Signals are sent simultane-
57:2241:135641:18:28:101:421:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ously, and are observed only by firms who have received them.
57:2242:135702:28:27:86:507:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.  Each firm makes an offer to at mostLworkers; offers are made simultaneously.
57:2243:135782:27:25:86:473:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.  Each worker accepts at most one offer from the set of offers she receives.
57:2244:135860:25:18:72:540:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Once again, sequential rationality ensures that workers will always select the best available
57:2245:135953:18:18:72:540:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:offer.   Hence,  we  take  this  behavior  for  workers  as  given  and  focus  on  the  reduced  game
57:2246:136055:18:18:72:240:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:consisting of the first two stages.
57:2247:136090:18:18:89:540:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A mixed strategy for workerwwhen deciding wether and to whom to send signals is a
57:2248:136171:18:18:72:540:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:map from the set of all possible preference lists to the set of distributions over subsets of
57:2249:136264:18:18:72:539:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:firms of sizeKor less that we denote as ∆(2FK), i.e.σw: Θw→∆(2FK).  Similarly, a mixed
57:2250:136350:18:18:72:539:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:strategy of firmfis a map from the set of all possible preference lists, Θf, and the set of
57:2251:136441:18:18:72:540:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:all possible combinations of received signals, 2W,to the set of distributions over subsets of
57:2252:136534:18:18:72:522:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers of sizeLor less, which we denote as ∆(2WL).  That is,σf: Θf×2W→∆(2WL).
57:2253:136612:18:18:89:539:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Preferences of both firms and workers are independently and uniformly chosen from all
57:2254:136697:18:18:72:539:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:possible preference orderings.  Similarly to Sections 3 and 4 we defineσW, σF, Σw,Σf,πw, and
57:2255:136789:18:18:72:540:89:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:πf.  The definition of sequential equilibrium and anonymous strategies can also be adopted
57:2256:136879:18:0:72:198:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in an analagous manner.
58:2257:136904:0:18:89:539:708:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We first consider an offer game without signals.  If firms use anonymous strategies, the
58:2258:136992:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:chances of hiring any worker, conditional on making her an offer, are the same.  Therefore,
58:2259:137083:18:18:72:539:672:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:each firm optimally makes its offers to theLhighest-ranked workers on its preference list.
58:2260:137173:18:18:72:540:654:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This is the unique symmetric equilibrium of the offer game without signals when firms use
58:2261:137262:18:18:72:294:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:anonymous strategies (see Proposition B3).
58:2262:137304:18:18:89:539:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We now turn to the analysis of the offer game with signals.  In any symmetric equilibrium
58:2263:137393:18:18:72:540:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in which workers send signals and signals are interpreted as a sign of interest by firms and
58:2264:137485:18:18:72:539:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:hence increase the chance of receiving an offer,  each worker sends herKsignals to herK
58:2265:137572:18:18:72:540:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:most preferred firms (see Proposition B4).  As in the case of one signal and each firm only
58:2266:137663:18:18:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:having one position, we pin down the behavior of workers in equilibrium:  workers send their
58:2267:137755:18:18:72:540:528:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signals to their highest ranked firms, and workers accept the best available offer.  We now
58:2268:137846:18:18:72:540:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:examine offers of firms in the second stage of the game, taking the strategies of workers and
58:2269:137939:18:18:72:338:492:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:beliefs of firms about interpreting signals as given.35
58:2270:137994:18:17:89:539:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In Section 4 each worker could send up to one signal, and each firm hadL= 1 positions
58:2271:138079:17:18:72:540:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to fill.  Then, when all other firms used anonymous strategies, firmfdecided between making
58:2272:138170:18:18:72:539:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:an offer tof’s most preferred workerTf(orT1f) andf’s most preferred worker in the subset of

58:2274:138349:18:18:72:539:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:make up toLoffers.  When deciding whom to make the first offer, firmf, once more, decides
58:2275:138438:18:18:72:540:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:between the most preferred workerTf(orT1f) and the most prefered worker among those

58:2278:138697:18:18:72:540:331:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cutoffj|WS|, thenfmakes an offer toS1fif and only if the rank ofS1fis lower or equal than
58:2279:138786:18:18:72:539:313:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:j|WS|.  If firmfmade an offer toS1f, then, for the second position, the firm decides between

58:2286:139350:18:18:72:540:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is  nowT2f,  the  overall  second  most  preferred  worker,  and  notT2f.   We  can  show  that  in
58:2287:139449:18:18:72:540:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:equilibrium, the cutoff forT2fwill be greater than forT1ffor any number if received signals
58:2288:139540:18:29:72:519:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(see Proposition B5).  We can now define the notion of cutoff strategies for this setting.
58:2289:139630:29:15:81:539:123:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:35Note that in any non-babbling symmetric equilibrium, all information sets for firms are realized with
58:2290:139733:15:12:72:540:108:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:positive probability.  Hence, the beliefs of firms are determined by Bayes’ Law:  if a firm receives a signal
58:2291:139842:12:12:72:539:96:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:from a worker, it believes that it is on of thekth top firms,k∈{1,...,K},in the workers’ preference list and
58:2292:139950:12:0:72:366:84:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:the probability of having rankkis identical across ranks{1,...,K}.
59:2293:140018:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:Definition B1(Cutoff Strategies in Case of Many Positions and Multiple Signals).Strategy

59:2303:140602:43:18:89:539:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We call (J1,...,JL)a cutoff matrixthat has cutoff vectors for each of the topLranked
59:2304:140686:18:18:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:workers  as  its  components.   Note  that  the  probability  of  a  firm’s  offer  being  accepted  by
59:2305:140789:18:18:72:540:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:any worker who has signaled to it is the same as in a symmetric equilibrium.  Similarly, the
59:2306:140881:18:18:72:540:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:probability of a firm’s offer being accepted by any worker who has not signaled to the firm
59:2307:140972:18:18:72:348:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is also the same across such workers (see Lemma B2).
59:2308:141024:18:18:89:539:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Using  an  argument  similar  to  the  case  of  one  position  and  one  signal,  we  show  that
59:2309:141121:18:18:72:540:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:cutoff strategies are optimal strategies for firms (see Proposition B6).  We can also impose
59:2310:141213:18:18:72:540:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a partial order on the cutoff strategies as in Section 4.  However, strategies of firms are no
59:2311:141307:18:17:72:540:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:longer necessarily strategic complements.  When other firms respond more to signals,  this
59:2312:141397:17:18:72:540:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:decreases the payoff from making an offer to both workers who have and workers who have
59:2313:141484:18:18:72:540:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:not signaled to the firm.  This is because receiving a signal does not guarantee acceptance in
59:2314:141578:18:18:72:540:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:case an offer is tendered to that worker.  We can, however, assure the existence of symmetric
59:2315:141671:18:28:72:214:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mixed strategy equilibrium.
59:2316:141698:28:18:72:540:265:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Theorem B1(Equilibrium Existence).There  exists  a  symmetric  equilibrium  of  the  offer
59:2317:141788:18:18:72:540:247:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:game  with  signals  where  1)  workers  send  their  signals  to  topKfirms,  and  2)  firms  play
59:2318:141887:18:28:72:212:229:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:symmetric cutoff strategies.
59:2319:141915:28:18:89:539:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We now address the welfare implications from the introduction of a signaling mechanism.
59:2320:142002:18:18:72:540:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Proposition B2 and Theorem B2 formally restate our welfare results from previous chapters
59:2321:142091:18:18:72:540:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for the case when firms have many positions and workers can send multiple signals.  The
59:2322:142178:18:18:72:540:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:logic of their proofs again begins with an incremental approach:  we first study the effect of
59:2323:142272:18:18:72:540:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a single firm increasing its cutoff, that is, responding more to signals.  We then rank various
59:2324:142367:18:17:72:540:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signaling equilibria in terms of their outcomes.  Finally, we show how the introduction of a
59:2325:142459:17:0:72:378:94:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:signaling mechanism impacts our three measures of welfare.
60:2326:142519:0:18:72:539:708:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Proposition B2(Welfare Across Equilibria).Consider  any  two  symmetric  cutoff  strategy
60:2327:142608:18:18:72:540:690:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:equilibria  where  in  one  equilibrium  firms  have  greater  cutoffs.  Compared  to  the  equilibrium
60:2328:142711:18:28:72:479:672:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:with lower cutoffs, in the equilibrium with greater cutoffs we have the following:
60:2329:142793:28:28:89:354:644:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f7:•the expected number of matches is weakly greater,
60:2330:142843:28:28:89:350:616:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f7:•workers have weakly higher expected payoffs, and
60:2331:142892:28:28:89:310:588:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f7:•firms have weakly lower expected payoffs.
60:2332:142934:28:18:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f7:Theorem B2(Welfare Impact of a Signaling Mechanism).Consider any non-babbling sym-
60:2333:143016:18:28:72:540:542:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:metric equilibrium of the offer game with signals.  Then the following three statements hold.
60:2334:143109:28:18:88:540:514:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:i.  The  expected  number  of  matches  is  strictly  greater  than  in  the  unique  equilibrium  of
60:2335:143210:18:28:101:258:496:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:the offer game with no signals.
60:2336:143241:28:17:84:539:468:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:ii.  The expected welfare of workers is strictly greater than in the unique equilibrium of the
60:2337:143335:17:28:101:239:451:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:offer game with no signals.
60:2338:143362:28:18:81:540:423:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:iii.  The  welfare  of  firms  may  be  greater  or  smaller  than  in  the  unique  equilibrium  of  the
60:2339:143467:18:39:101:239:405:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f7:offer game with no signals.
